I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
bug(sandbox): Landlock not enforced on Landlock-capable kernels — best_effort silently returns Ok()
## Summary

OpenShell 0.0.26 does not enforce Landlock filesystem restrictions despite receiving a correct policy and running on Landlock-capable kernels. The sandbox process runs as `unconfined` (`/proc/1/attr/current = "unconfined"`). `/sandbox` is fully writable.

Reported by QA in [NVIDIA/NemoClaw#1739](https://github.com/NVIDIA/NemoClaw/issues/1739) / [nvbug 6066573](https://nvbugspro.nvidia.com/bug/6066573).

**Previous issues [#584](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/issues/584) and [#664](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/issues/664) were closed as fixed (PRs [#599](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/pull/599), [#677](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/pull/677)), and those fixes shipped in v0.0.26, but the problem persists.**

v0.0.27 has no Landlock changes over v0.0.26.

## Environment (from QA)

All platforms affected:
- **Brev GPU**: kernel 5.15.0-107, kernel 6.8.0-57
- **Standard Ubuntu**: kernel 6.8.0-57
- `CONFIG_SECURITY_LANDLOCK=y`
- Landlock in LSM: `lockdown,capability,landlock,yama,apparmor`
- OpenShell: 0.0.26

Kernels are well above 5.13 (Landlock V1) and 5.19 (unprivileged Landlock). This is not a kernel compatibility issue.

## Reproduction

```bash
nemoclaw onboard
nemoclaw <name> connect
touch /sandbox/testfile  # Expected: Permission denied. Actual: succeeds
cat /proc/1/attr/current # Shows: "unconfined"
```

## Policy delivered correctly

`nemoclaw status --json` confirms:

```yaml
filesystem_policy:
  include_workdir: false
  read_only:
    - /sandbox
    - /sandbox/.openclaw
  read_write:
    - /tmp
    - /sandbox/.openclaw-data
    - /sandbox/.nemoclaw
landlock:
  compatibility: best_effort
```

## Root cause analysis

### Execution order in [process.rs#L184-L187](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/process.rs#L184):

```rust
drop_privileges(&policy)                       // line 184: switches to sandbox user (uid 998)
sandbox::apply(&policy, workdir.as_deref())    // line 187: tries to apply Landlock AS UNPRIVILEGED USER
```

### Inside [landlock.rs](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs):

1. `ruleset.create()` — [line 60](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs#L60)
2. `try_open_path()` for each policy path — [lines 63-80](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs#L63)
3. `restrict_self()` — [line 103](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs#L103)

If ANY step fails and `compatibility == BestEffort`, the error is caught at [line 107](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs#L107), an OCSF finding is logged, and **`Ok(())` is returned at [line 128](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs#L128)**. The caller sees success. The sandbox runs unconfined.

## Likely failure candidates

### 1. `try_open_path()` fails after `drop_privileges()` (MOST LIKELY)

`try_open_path()` does `open(path, O_PATH | O_CLOEXEC)` as the **sandbox user (uid 998)**, not root. Container runtimes, AppArmor profiles, or mount configurations may restrict `O_PATH` opens for non-root users. If ALL paths fail, `rules_applied == 0` at [line 83](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs#L83) → error → `best_effort` catches it → `Ok(())` → unconfined.

**Fix:** Open path FDs as root BEFORE `drop_privileges()`, then pass them into the Landlock ruleset builder.

### 2. Container runtime seccomp blocks Landlock syscalls

Docker's default seccomp profile may block syscalls 444 (`landlock_create_ruleset`), 445 (`landlock_add_rule`), 446 (`landlock_restrict_self`). This would cause `ruleset.create()` at [line 60](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs#L60) to fail before OpenShell's own seccomp runs.

**Fix:** Verify the container runtime permits Landlock syscalls, or document the requirement.

### 3. `landlock` crate ABI negotiation failure

The code uses `ABI::V2` at [line 33](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs#L33) with `CompatLevel::BestEffort`. The crate (v0.4.4) might fail ABI negotiation internally despite kernel support.

### 4. `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` not set

`restrict_self()` requires `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS`. If Docker's `--security-opt no-new-privileges` isn't set and the code doesn't call `prctl()` explicitly, `restrict_self()` fails with EPERM.

## Suggested fixes

1. **Move path FD opening before `drop_privileges()`** — open `O_PATH` FDs as root, pass them into the ruleset builder. This is the most likely fix for candidate 1.

2. **Make the failure visible** — the OCSF finding at [line 125](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/blob/main/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/sandbox/linux/landlock.rs#L125) goes to structured logs nobody reads. Add a visible stderr warning and/or set an env var like `OPENSHELL_LANDLOCK_ACTIVE=0` so downstream code can detect it.

3. **Log the specific error** — the OCSF finding includes the error string, but it's buried in structured logging. Print the actual failure reason to stderr so operators can diagnose which candidate is failing.

4. **Two-phase Landlock** — phase 1 (as root): open path FDs + create ruleset. Phase 2 (after `drop_privileges()`): call `restrict_self()` only.

## Impact

- NemoClaw's entire Landlock-based security model ([PR #1121](https://github.com/NVIDIA/NemoClaw/pull/1121)) is ineffective
- `nemoclaw onboard` displays "Landlock + seccomp + netns" which is misleading
- Only DAC protections (root:root, sticky bit, chmod 444) prevent filesystem abuse

## Related

- [NVIDIA/NemoClaw#1739](https://github.com/NVIDIA/NemoClaw/issues/1739) / [nvbug 6066573](https://nvbugspro.nvidia.com/bug/6066573)
- Closed (fixes in v0.0.26 but problem persists): [#584](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/issues/584), [#664](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/issues/664)
- Related: [#783](https://github.com/NVIDIA/OpenShell/issues/783) (prepare_filesystem chowns read_write dirs)

     4	//! Process management and signal handling.
     5	
     6	use crate::child_env;
     7	use crate::policy::{NetworkMode, SandboxPolicy};
     8	use crate::sandbox;
     9	#[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
    10	use crate::sandbox::linux::netns::NetworkNamespace;
    11	#[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
    12	use crate::{register_managed_child, unregister_managed_child};
    13	use miette::{IntoDiagnostic, Result};
    14	use nix::sys::signal::{self, Signal};
    15	use nix::unistd::{Group, Pid, User};
    16	use std::collections::HashMap;
    17	use std::ffi::CString;

    25	const SSH_HANDSHAKE_SECRET_ENV: &str = "OPENSHELL_SSH_HANDSHAKE_SECRET";
    26	
    27	fn inject_provider_env(cmd: &mut Command, provider_env: &HashMap<String, String>) {
    28	    for (key, value) in provider_env {
    29	        cmd.env(key, value);
    30	    }
    31	}
    32	
    33	fn scrub_sensitive_env(cmd: &mut Command) {
    34	    cmd.env_remove(SSH_HANDSHAKE_SECRET_ENV);
    35	}
    36	
    37	/// Handle to a running process.
    38	pub struct ProcessHandle {
    39	    child: Child,
    40	    pid: u32,
    41	}
    42	
    43	impl ProcessHandle {
    44	    /// Spawn a new process.
    45	    ///
    46	    /// # Errors
    47	    ///
    48	    /// Returns an error if the process fails to start.
    49	    #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
    50	    #[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
    51	    pub fn spawn(
    52	        program: &str,
    53	        args: &[String],
    54	        workdir: Option<&str>,
    55	        interactive: bool,
    56	        policy: &SandboxPolicy,
    57	        netns: Option<&NetworkNamespace>,
    58	        ca_paths: Option<&(PathBuf, PathBuf)>,
    59	        provider_env: &HashMap<String, String>,
    60	    ) -> Result<Self> {
    61	        Self::spawn_impl(
    62	            program,
    63	            args,
    64	            workdir,
    65	            interactive,
    66	            policy,
    67	            netns.and_then(NetworkNamespace::ns_fd),
    68	            ca_paths,
    69	            provider_env,
    70	        )
    71	    }
    72	
    73	    /// Spawn a new process (non-Linux platforms).
    74	    ///
    75	    /// # Errors
    76	    ///
    77	    /// Returns an error if the process fails to start.
    78	    #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
    79	    pub fn spawn(
    80	        program: &str,
    81	        args: &[String],
    82	        workdir: Option<&str>,
    83	        interactive: bool,
    84	        policy: &SandboxPolicy,
    85	        ca_paths: Option<&(PathBuf, PathBuf)>,
    86	        provider_env: &HashMap<String, String>,
    87	    ) -> Result<Self> {
    88	        Self::spawn_impl(
    89	            program,
    90	            args,
    91	            workdir,
    92	            interactive,
    93	            policy,
    94	            ca_paths,
    95	            provider_env,
    96	        )
    97	    }
    98	
    99	    #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
   100	    #[allow(clippy::too_many_arguments)]
   101	    fn spawn_impl(
   102	        program: &str,
   103	        args: &[String],
   104	        workdir: Option<&str>,
   105	        interactive: bool,
   106	        policy: &SandboxPolicy,
   107	        netns_fd: Option<RawFd>,
   108	        ca_paths: Option<&(PathBuf, PathBuf)>,
   109	        provider_env: &HashMap<String, String>,
   110	    ) -> Result<Self> {
   111	        let mut cmd = Command::new(program);
   112	        cmd.args(args)
   113	            .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
   114	            .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
   115	            .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
   116	            .kill_on_drop(true)
   117	            .env("OPENSHELL_SANDBOX", "1");
   118	
   119	        scrub_sensitive_env(&mut cmd);
   120	        inject_provider_env(&mut cmd, provider_env);
   121	
   122	        if let Some(dir) = workdir {
   123	            cmd.current_dir(dir);
   124	        }
   125	
   126	        if matches!(policy.network.mode, NetworkMode::Proxy) {
   127	            let proxy = policy.network.proxy.as_ref().ok_or_else(|| {
   128	                miette::miette!(
   129	                    "Network mode is set to proxy but no proxy configuration was provided"
   130	                )
   131	            })?;
   132	            // When using network namespace, set proxy URL to the veth host IP
   133	            if netns_fd.is_some() {
   134	                // The proxy is on 10.200.0.1:3128 (or configured port)
   135	                let port = proxy.http_addr.map_or(3128, |addr| addr.port());
   136	                let proxy_url = format!("http://10.200.0.1:{port}");
   137	                // Both uppercase and lowercase variants: curl/wget use uppercase,
   138	                // gRPC C-core (libgrpc) checks lowercase http_proxy/https_proxy.
   139	                for (key, value) in child_env::proxy_env_vars(&proxy_url) {
   140	                    cmd.env(key, value);
   141	                }
   142	            } else if let Some(http_addr) = proxy.http_addr {
   143	                let proxy_url = format!("http://{http_addr}");
   144	                for (key, value) in child_env::proxy_env_vars(&proxy_url) {
   145	                    cmd.env(key, value);
   146	                }
   147	            }
   148	        }
   149	
   150	        // Set TLS trust store env vars so sandbox processes trust the ephemeral CA
   151	        if let Some((ca_cert_path, combined_bundle_path)) = ca_paths {
   152	            for (key, value) in child_env::tls_env_vars(ca_cert_path, combined_bundle_path) {
   153	                cmd.env(key, value);
   154	            }
   155	        }
   156	
   157	        // Set up process group for signal handling (non-interactive mode only).
   158	        // In interactive mode, we inherit the parent's process group to maintain
   159	        // proper terminal control for shells and interactive programs.
   160	        // SAFETY: pre_exec runs after fork but before exec in the child process.
   161	        // setpgid and setns are async-signal-safe and safe to call in this context.
   162	        {
   163	            let policy = policy.clone();
   164	            let workdir = workdir.map(str::to_string);
   165	            #[allow(unsafe_code)]
   166	            unsafe {
   167	                cmd.pre_exec(move || {
   168	                    if !interactive {
   169	                        // Create new process group
   170	                        libc::setpgid(0, 0);
   171	                    }
   172	
   173	                    // Enter network namespace before applying other restrictions
   174	                    if let Some(fd) = netns_fd {
   175	                        let result = libc::setns(fd, libc::CLONE_NEWNET);
   176	                        if result != 0 {
   177	                            return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
   178	                        }
   179	                    }
   180	
   181	                    // Drop privileges before applying sandbox restrictions.
   182	                    // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
   183	                    // which may be blocked by Landlock.
   184	                    drop_privileges(&policy)
   185	                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
   186	
   187	                    sandbox::apply(&policy, workdir.as_deref())
   188	                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
   189	
   190	                    Ok(())
   191	                });
   192	            }
   193	        }
   194	
   195	        let child = cmd.spawn().into_diagnostic()?;
   196	        let pid = child.id().unwrap_or(0);
   197	        register_managed_child(pid);
   198	
   199	        debug!(pid, program, "Process spawned");
   200	
   201	        Ok(Self { child, pid })
   202	    }
   203	
   204	    #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
   205	    fn spawn_impl(
   206	        program: &str,
   207	        args: &[String],
   208	        workdir: Option<&str>,
   209	        interactive: bool,
   210	        policy: &SandboxPolicy,
   211	        ca_paths: Option<&(PathBuf, PathBuf)>,
   212	        provider_env: &HashMap<String, String>,
   213	    ) -> Result<Self> {
   214	        let mut cmd = Command::new(program);
   215	        cmd.args(args)
   216	            .stdin(Stdio::inherit())
   217	            .stdout(Stdio::inherit())
   218	            .stderr(Stdio::inherit())
   219	            .kill_on_drop(true)
   220	            .env("OPENSHELL_SANDBOX", "1");
   221	
   222	        scrub_sensitive_env(&mut cmd);
   223	        inject_provider_env(&mut cmd, provider_env);
   224	
   225	        if let Some(dir) = workdir {
   226	            cmd.current_dir(dir);
   227	        }
   228	
   229	        if matches!(policy.network.mode, NetworkMode::Proxy) {
   230	            let proxy = policy.network.proxy.as_ref().ok_or_else(|| {
   231	                miette::miette!(
   232	                    "Network mode is set to proxy but no proxy configuration was provided"
   233	                )
   234	            })?;
   235	            if let Some(http_addr) = proxy.http_addr {
   236	                let proxy_url = format!("http://{http_addr}");
   237	                for (key, value) in child_env::proxy_env_vars(&proxy_url) {
   238	                    cmd.env(key, value);
   239	                }
   240	            }
   241	        }
   242	
   243	        // Set TLS trust store env vars so sandbox processes trust the ephemeral CA
   244	        if let Some((ca_cert_path, combined_bundle_path)) = ca_paths {
   245	            for (key, value) in child_env::tls_env_vars(ca_cert_path, combined_bundle_path) {
   246	                cmd.env(key, value);
   247	            }
   248	        }
   249	
   250	        // Set up process group for signal handling (non-interactive mode only).
   251	        // In interactive mode, we inherit the parent's process group to maintain
   252	        // proper terminal control for shells and interactive programs.
   253	        // SAFETY: pre_exec runs after fork but before exec in the child process.
   254	        // setpgid is async-signal-safe and safe to call in this context.
   255	        #[cfg(unix)]
   256	        {
   257	            let policy = policy.clone();
   258	            let workdir = workdir.map(str::to_string);
   259	            #[allow(unsafe_code)]
   260	            unsafe {
   261	                cmd.pre_exec(move || {
   262	                    if !interactive {
   263	                        // Create new process group
   264	                        libc::setpgid(0, 0);
   265	                    }
   266	
   267	                    // Drop privileges before applying sandbox restrictions.
   268	                    // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
   269	                    // which may be blocked by Landlock.
   270	                    drop_privileges(&policy)
   271	                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
   272	
   273	                    sandbox::apply(&policy, workdir.as_deref())
   274	                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
   275	
   276	                    Ok(())
   277	                });
   278	            }
   279	        }
   280	
   281	        let child = cmd.spawn().into_diagnostic()?;
   282	        let pid = child.id().unwrap_or(0);
   283	        #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
   284	        register_managed_child(pid);
   285	
   286	        debug!(pid, program, "Process spawned");
   287	
   288	        Ok(Self { child, pid })
   289	    }
   290	
   291	    /// Get the process ID.
   292	    #[must_use]
   293	    pub const fn pid(&self) -> u32 {
   294	        self.pid
   295	    }
   296	
   297	    /// Wait for the process to exit.
   298	    ///
   299	    /// # Errors
   300	    ///
   301	    /// Returns an error if waiting fails.
   302	    pub async fn wait(&mut self) -> std::io::Result<ProcessStatus> {
   303	        let status = self.child.wait().await;
   304	        #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
   305	        unregister_managed_child(self.pid);
   306	        let status = status?;
   307	        Ok(ProcessStatus::from(status))
   308	    }
   309	
   310	    /// Send a signal to the process.
   311	    ///
   312	    /// # Errors
   313	    ///
   314	    /// Returns an error if the signal cannot be sent.
   315	    pub fn signal(&self, sig: Signal) -> Result<()> {
   316	        let pid = i32::try_from(self.pid).unwrap_or(i32::MAX);
   317	        signal::kill(Pid::from_raw(pid), sig).into_diagnostic()
   318	    }
   319	
   320	    /// Kill the process.
   321	    ///
   322	    /// # Errors
   323	    ///
   324	    /// Returns an error if the process cannot be killed.
   325	    pub fn kill(&mut self) -> Result<()> {
   326	        // First try SIGTERM
   327	        if let Err(e) = self.signal(Signal::SIGTERM) {
   328	            openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
   329	                openshell_ocsf::ProcessActivityBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
   330	                    .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Close)
   331	                    .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Medium)
   332	                    .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Failure)
   333	                    .message(format!("Failed to send SIGTERM: {e}"))
   334	                    .build()
   335	            );
   336	        }
   337	
   338	        // Give the process a moment to terminate gracefully
   339	        std::thread::sleep(std::time::Duration::from_millis(100));
   340	
   341	        // Force kill if still running
   342	        if let Some(id) = self.child.id() {
   343	            debug!(pid = id, "Sending SIGKILL");
   344	            let pid = i32::try_from(id).unwrap_or(i32::MAX);
   345	            let _ = signal::kill(Pid::from_raw(pid), Signal::SIGKILL);
   346	        }
   347	
   348	        Ok(())
   349	    }
   350	}
   351	
   352	impl Drop for ProcessHandle {
   353	    fn drop(&mut self) {
   354	        #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
   355	        unregister_managed_child(self.pid);
   356	    }
   357	}
   358	
   359	#[cfg(unix)]
   360	pub fn drop_privileges(policy: &SandboxPolicy) -> Result<()> {
   361	    let user_name = match policy.process.run_as_user.as_deref() {
   362	        Some(name) if !name.is_empty() => Some(name),
   363	        _ => None,
   364	    };
   365	    let group_name = match policy.process.run_as_group.as_deref() {
   366	        Some(name) if !name.is_empty() => Some(name),
   367	        _ => None,
   368	    };
   369	
   370	    // If no user/group is configured and we are running as root, fall back to
   371	    // "sandbox:sandbox" instead of silently keeping root.  This covers the
   372	    // local/dev-mode path where policies are loaded from disk and never pass
   373	    // through the server-side `ensure_sandbox_process_identity` normalization.
   374	    // For non-root runtimes, the no-op is safe -- we are already unprivileged.
   375	    if user_name.is_none() && group_name.is_none() {
   376	        if nix::unistd::geteuid().is_root() {
   377	            let mut fallback = policy.clone();
   378	            fallback.process.run_as_user = Some("sandbox".into());
   379	            fallback.process.run_as_group = Some("sandbox".into());
   380	            return drop_privileges(&fallback);
   381	        }
   382	        return Ok(());
   383	    }
   384	
   385	    let user = if let Some(name) = user_name {
   386	        User::from_name(name)
   387	            .into_diagnostic()?
   388	            .ok_or_else(|| miette::miette!("Sandbox user not found: {name}"))?
   389	    } else {
   390	        User::from_uid(nix::unistd::geteuid())
   391	            .into_diagnostic()?
   392	            .ok_or_else(|| miette::miette!("Failed to resolve current user"))?
   393	    };
   394	
   395	    let group = if let Some(name) = group_name {
   396	        Group::from_name(name)
   397	            .into_diagnostic()?
   398	            .ok_or_else(|| miette::miette!("Sandbox group not found: {name}"))?
   399	    } else {
   400	        Group::from_gid(user.gid)
   401	            .into_diagnostic()?
   402	            .ok_or_else(|| miette::miette!("Failed to resolve user primary group"))?
   403	    };
   404	
   405	    if user_name.is_some() {
   406	        let user_cstr =
   407	            CString::new(user.name.clone()).map_err(|_| miette::miette!("Invalid user name"))?;
   408	        #[cfg(any(
   409	            target_os = "macos",
   410	            target_os = "ios",
   411	            target_os = "haiku",
   412	            target_os = "redox"
   413	        ))]
   414	        {
   415	            let _ = user_cstr;
   416	        }
   417	        #[cfg(not(any(
   418	            target_os = "macos",
   419	            target_os = "ios",
   420	            target_os = "haiku",
   421	            target_os = "redox"
   422	        )))]
   423	        {
   424	            nix::unistd::initgroups(user_cstr.as_c_str(), group.gid).into_diagnostic()?;
   425	        }
   426	    }
   427	
   428	    nix::unistd::setgid(group.gid).into_diagnostic()?;
   429	
   430	    // Verify effective GID actually changed (defense-in-depth, CWE-250 / CERT POS37-C)
   431	    let effective_gid = nix::unistd::getegid();
   432	    if effective_gid != group.gid {
   433	        return Err(miette::miette!(
   434	            "Privilege drop verification failed: expected effective GID {}, got {}",
   435	            group.gid,
   436	            effective_gid
   437	        ));
   438	    }
   439	
   440	    if user_name.is_some() {
   441	        nix::unistd::setuid(user.uid).into_diagnostic()?;
   442	
   443	        // Verify effective UID actually changed (defense-in-depth, CWE-250 / CERT POS37-C)
   444	        let effective_uid = nix::unistd::geteuid();
   445	        if effective_uid != user.uid {
   446	            return Err(miette::miette!(
   447	                "Privilege drop verification failed: expected effective UID {}, got {}",
   448	                user.uid,
   449	                effective_uid
   450	            ));
   451	        }
   452	
   453	        // Verify root cannot be re-acquired (CERT POS37-C hardening).
   454	        // If we dropped from root, setuid(0) must fail; success means privileges
   455	        // were not fully relinquished.
   456	        if nix::unistd::setuid(nix::unistd::Uid::from_raw(0)).is_ok() && user.uid.as_raw() != 0 {
   457	            return Err(miette::miette!(
   458	                "Privilege drop verification failed: process can still re-acquire root (UID 0)<response clipped><NOTE>To save on context only part of this file has been shown to you. You should retry this tool after you have searched inside the file with `grep -n` in order to find the line numbers of what you are looking for.</NOTE>

     4	//! Landlock filesystem sandboxing.
     5	
     6	use crate::policy::{LandlockCompatibility, SandboxPolicy};
     7	use landlock::{
     8	    ABI, Access, AccessFs, CompatLevel, Compatible, PathBeneath, PathFd, PathFdError, Ruleset,
     9	    RulesetAttr, RulesetCreatedAttr,
    10	};
    11	use miette::{IntoDiagnostic, Result};
    12	use std::path::{Path, PathBuf};
    13	use tracing::debug;
    14	
    15	pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    16	    let read_only = policy.filesystem.read_only.clone();
    17	    let mut read_write = policy.filesystem.read_write.clone();
    18	
    19	    if policy.filesystem.include_workdir
    20	        && let Some(dir) = workdir
    21	    {
    22	        let workdir_path = PathBuf::from(dir);
    23	        if !read_write.contains(&workdir_path) {
    24	            read_write.push(workdir_path);
    25	        }
    26	    }
    27	
    28	    if read_only.is_empty() && read_write.is_empty() {
    29	        return Ok(());
    30	    }
    31	
    32	    let total_paths = read_only.len() + read_write.len();
    33	    let abi = ABI::V2;
    34	    openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
    35	        openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
    36	            .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
    37	            .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
    38	            .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "applying")
    39	            .message(format!(
    40	                "Applying Landlock filesystem sandbox [abi:{abi:?} compat:{:?} ro:{} rw:{}]",
    41	                policy.landlock.compatibility,
    42	                read_only.len(),
    43	                read_write.len(),
    44	            ))
    45	            .build()
    46	    );
    47	
    48	    let compatibility = &policy.landlock.compatibility;
    49	
    50	    let result: Result<()> = (|| {
    51	        let access_all = AccessFs::from_all(abi);
    52	        let access_read = AccessFs::from_read(abi);
    53	
    54	        let mut ruleset = Ruleset::default();
    55	        ruleset = ruleset
    56	            .set_compatibility(compat_level(compatibility))
    57	            .handle_access(access_all)
    58	            .into_diagnostic()?;
    59	
    60	        let mut ruleset = ruleset.create().into_diagnostic()?;
    61	        let mut rules_applied: usize = 0;
    62	
    63	        for path in &read_only {
    64	            if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, compatibility)? {
    65	                debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-only");
    66	                ruleset = ruleset
    67	                    .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_read))
    68	                    .into_diagnostic()?;
    69	                rules_applied += 1;
    70	            }
    71	        }
    72	
    73	        for path in &read_write {
    74	            if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, compatibility)? {
    75	                debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-write");
    76	                ruleset = ruleset
    77	                    .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_all))
    78	                    .into_diagnostic()?;
    79	                rules_applied += 1;
    80	            }
    81	        }
    82	
    83	        if rules_applied == 0 {
    84	            return Err(miette::miette!(
    85	                "Landlock ruleset has zero valid paths — all {} path(s) failed to open. \
    86	                 Refusing to apply an empty ruleset that would block all filesystem access.",
    87	                total_paths,
    88	            ));
    89	        }
    90	
    91	        let skipped = total_paths - rules_applied;
    92	        openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
    93	            openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
    94	                .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
    95	                .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
    96	                .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "built")
    97	                .message(format!(
    98	                    "Landlock ruleset built [rules_applied:{rules_applied} skipped:{skipped}]"
    99	                ))
   100	                .build()
   101	        );
   102	
   103	        ruleset.restrict_self().into_diagnostic()?;
   104	        Ok(())
   105	    })();
   106	
   107	    if let Err(err) = result {
   108	        if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
   109	            openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
   110	                openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
   111	                    .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
   112	                    .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
   113	                    .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
   114	                    .is_alert(true)
   115	                    .finding_info(
   116	                        openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
   117	                            "landlock-unavailable",
   118	                            "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
   119	                        )
   120	                        .with_desc(&format!(
   121	                            "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
   122	                             Set landlock.compatibility to 'hard_requirement' to make this fatal."
   123	                        )),
   124	                    )
   125	                    .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
   126	                    .build()
   127	            );
   128	            return Ok(());
   129	        }
   130	        return Err(err);
   131	    }
   132	
   133	    Ok(())
   134	}

   136	/// Attempt to open a path for Landlock rule creation.
   137	///
   138	/// In `BestEffort` mode, inaccessible paths (missing, permission denied, symlink
   139	/// loops, etc.) are skipped with a warning and `Ok(None)` is returned so the
   140	/// caller can continue building the ruleset from the remaining valid paths.
   141	///
   142	/// In `HardRequirement` mode, any failure is fatal — the caller propagates the
   143	/// error, which ultimately aborts sandbox startup.
   144	fn try_open_path(path: &Path, compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility) -> Result<Option<PathFd>> {
   145	    match PathFd::new(path) {
   146	        Ok(fd) => Ok(Some(fd)),
   147	        Err(err) => {
   148	            let reason = classify_path_fd_error(&err);
   149	            let is_not_found = matches!(
   150	                &err,
   151	                PathFdError::OpenCall { source, .. }
   152	                    if source.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::NotFound
   153	            );
   154	            match compatibility {
   155	                LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort => {
   156	                    // NotFound is expected for stale baseline paths (e.g.
   157	                    // /app baked into the server-stored policy but absent
   158	                    // in this container image).  Log at debug! to avoid
   159	                    // polluting SSH exec stdout — the pre_exec hook
   160	                    // inherits the tracing subscriber whose writer targets
   161	                    // fd 1 (the pipe/PTY).
   162	                    //
   163	                    // Other errors (permission denied, symlink loops, etc.)
   164	                    // are genuinely unexpected and logged at warn!.
   165	                    if is_not_found {
   166	                        debug!(
   167	                            path = %path.display(),
   168	                            reason,
   169	                            "Skipping non-existent Landlock path (best-effort mode)"
   170	                        );
   171	                    } else {
   172	                        openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
   173	                            openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
   174	                                .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Medium)
   175	                                .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Failure)
   176	                                .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Other, "degraded")
   177	                                .message(format!(
   178	                                    "Skipping inaccessible Landlock path (best-effort) [path:{} error:{err}]",
   179	                                    path.display()
   180	                                ))
   181	                                .build()
   182	                        );
   183	                    }
   184	                    Ok(None)
   185	                }
   186	                LandlockCompatibility::HardRequirement => Err(miette::miette!(
   187	                    "Landlock path unavailable in hard_requirement mode: {} ({}): {}",
   188	                    path.display(),
   189	                    reason,
   190	                    err,
   191	                )),
   192	            }
   193	        }
   194	    }
   195	}
   196	
   197	/// Classify a [`PathFdError`] into a human-readable reason.
   198	///
   199	/// `PathFd::new()` wraps `open(path, O_PATH | O_CLOEXEC)` which can fail for
   200	/// several reasons beyond simple non-existence. The `PathFdError::OpenCall`
   201	/// variant wraps the underlying `std::io::Error`.
   202	fn classify_path_fd_error(err: &PathFdError) -> &'static str {
   203	    match err {
   204	        PathFdError::OpenCall { source, .. } => classify_io_error(source),
   205	        // PathFdError is #[non_exhaustive], handle future variants gracefully.
   206	        _ => "unexpected error",
   207	    }
   208	}
   209	
   210	/// Classify a `std::io::Error` into a human-readable reason string.
   211	fn classify_io_error(err: &std::io::Error) -> &'static str {
   212	    match err.kind() {
   213	        std::io::ErrorKind::NotFound => "path does not exist",
   214	        std::io::ErrorKind::PermissionDenied => "permission denied",
   215	        _ => match err.raw_os_error() {
   216	            Some(40) => "too many symlink levels",           // ELOOP
   217	            Some(36) => "path name too long",                // ENAMETOOLONG
   218	            Some(20) => "path component is not a directory", // ENOTDIR
   219	            _ => "unexpected error",
   220	        },
   221	    }
   222	}
   223	
   224	fn compat_level(level: &LandlockCompatibility) -> CompatLevel {
   225	    match level {
   226	        LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort => CompatLevel::BestEffort,
   227	        LandlockCompatibility::HardRequirement => CompatLevel::HardRequirement,
   228	    }
   229	}

    13	///
    14	/// # Errors
    15	///
    16	/// Returns an error if the sandbox cannot be applied.
    17	#[cfg_attr(not(target_os = "linux"), allow(clippy::unnecessary_wraps))]

     1	// SPDX-FileCopyrightText: Copyright (c) 2025-2026 NVIDIA CORPORATION & AFFILIATES. All rights reserved.
     2	// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0
     3	
     4	//! Shared sandbox policy parsing and defaults for OpenShell.
     5	//!
     6	//! Provides bidirectional YAML↔proto conversion for sandbox policies.
     7	//!
     8	//! The serde types here are the **single canonical representation** of the YAML
     9	//! policy schema. Both parsing (YAML→proto) and serialization (proto→YAML) use
    10	//! these types, ensuring round-trip fidelity.
    11	
    12	use std::collections::{BTreeMap, HashMap};
    13	use std::fmt;
    14	use std::path::Path;
    15	
    16	use miette::{IntoDiagnostic, Result, WrapErr};
    17	use openshell_core::proto::{
    18	    FilesystemPolicy, L7Allow, L7QueryMatcher, L7Rule, LandlockPolicy, NetworkBinary,
    19	    NetworkEndpoint, NetworkPolicyRule, ProcessPolicy, SandboxPolicy,
    20	};
    21	use serde::{Deserialize, Serialize};
    22	
    23	// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    24	// YAML serde types (canonical — used for both parsing and serialization)
    25	// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
    26	
    27	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
    28	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
    29	struct PolicyFile {
    30	    version: u32,
    31	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Option::is_none")]
    32	    filesystem_policy: Option<FilesystemDef>,
    33	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Option::is_none")]
    34	    landlock: Option<LandlockDef>,
    35	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Option::is_none")]
    36	    process: Option<ProcessDef>,
    37	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "BTreeMap::is_empty")]
    38	    network_policies: BTreeMap<String, NetworkPolicyRuleDef>,
    39	}
    40	
    41	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
    42	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
    43	struct FilesystemDef {
    44	    #[serde(default)]
    45	    include_workdir: bool,
    46	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Vec::is_empty")]
    47	    read_only: Vec<String>,
    48	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Vec::is_empty")]
    49	    read_write: Vec<String>,
    50	}
    51	
    52	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
    53	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
    54	struct LandlockDef {
    55	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
    56	    compatibility: String,
    57	}
    58	
    59	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
    60	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
    61	struct ProcessDef {
    62	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
    63	    run_as_user: String,
    64	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
    65	    run_as_group: String,
    66	}
    67	
    68	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
    69	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
    70	struct NetworkPolicyRuleDef {
    71	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
    72	    name: String,
    73	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Vec::is_empty")]
    74	    endpoints: Vec<NetworkEndpointDef>,
    75	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Vec::is_empty")]
    76	    binaries: Vec<NetworkBinaryDef>,
    77	}
    78	
    79	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
    80	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
    81	struct NetworkEndpointDef {
    82	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
    83	    host: String,
    84	    /// Single port (backwards compat). Mutually exclusive with `ports`.
    85	    /// Uses `u16` to reject invalid values >65535 at parse time.
    86	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "is_zero")]
    87	    port: u16,
    88	    /// Multiple ports. When non-empty, this endpoint covers all listed ports.
    89	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Vec::is_empty")]
    90	    ports: Vec<u16>,
    91	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
    92	    protocol: String,
    93	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
    94	    tls: String,
    95	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
    96	    enforcement: String,
    97	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
    98	    access: String,
    99	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Vec::is_empty")]
   100	    rules: Vec<L7RuleDef>,
   101	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Vec::is_empty")]
   102	    allowed_ips: Vec<String>,
   103	}
   104	
   105	fn is_zero(v: &u16) -> bool {
   106	    *v == 0
   107	}
   108	
   109	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
   110	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
   111	struct L7RuleDef {
   112	    allow: L7AllowDef,
   113	}
   114	
   115	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
   116	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
   117	struct L7AllowDef {
   118	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
   119	    method: String,
   120	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
   121	    path: String,
   122	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "String::is_empty")]
   123	    command: String,
   124	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "BTreeMap::is_empty")]
   125	    query: BTreeMap<String, QueryMatcherDef>,
   126	}
   127	
   128	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
   129	#[serde(untagged)]
   130	enum QueryMatcherDef {
   131	    Glob(String),
   132	    Any(QueryAnyDef),
   133	}
   134	
   135	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
   136	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
   137	struct QueryAnyDef {
   138	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing_if = "Vec::is_empty")]
   139	    any: Vec<String>,
   140	}
   141	
   142	#[derive(Debug, Serialize, Deserialize)]
   143	#[serde(deny_unknown_fields)]
   144	struct NetworkBinaryDef {
   145	    path: String,
   146	    /// Deprecated: ignored. Kept for backward compat with existing YAML files.
   147	    #[serde(default, skip_serializing)]
   148	    #[allow(dead_code)]
   149	    harness: bool,
   150	}
   151	
   152	// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   153	// YAML → proto conversion
   154	// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   155	
   156	fn to_proto(raw: PolicyFile) -> SandboxPolicy {
   157	    let network_policies = raw
   158	        .network_policies
   159	        .into_iter()
   160	        .map(|(key, rule)| {
   161	            let proto_rule = NetworkPolicyRule {
   162	                name: if rule.name.is_empty() {
   163	                    key.clone()
   164	                } else {
   165	                    rule.name
   166	                },
   167	                endpoints: rule
   168	                    .endpoints
   169	                    .into_iter()
   170	                    .map(|e| {
   171	                        // Normalize port/ports: ports takes precedence, else
   172	                        // single port is promoted to ports array.
   173	                        let normalized_ports: Vec<u32> = if !e.ports.is_empty() {
   174	                            e.ports.into_iter().map(u32::from).collect()
   175	                        } else if e.port > 0 {
   176	                            vec![u32::from(e.port)]
   177	                        } else {
   178	                            vec![]
   179	                        };
   180	                        NetworkEndpoint {
   181	                            host: e.host,
   182	                            port: normalized_ports.first().copied().unwrap_or(0),
   183	                            ports: normalized_ports,
   184	                            protocol: e.protocol,
   185	                            tls: e.tls,
   186	                            enforcement: e.enforcement,
   187	                            access: e.access,
   188	                            rules: e
   189	                                .rules
   190	                                .into_iter()
   191	                                .map(|r| L7Rule {
   192	                                    allow: Some(L7Allow {
   193	                                        method: r.allow.method,
   194	                                        path: r.allow.path,
   195	                                        command: r.allow.command,
   196	                                        query: r
   197	                                            .allow
   198	                                            .query
   199	                                            .into_iter()
   200	                                            .map(|(key, matcher)| {
   201	                                                let proto = match matcher {
   202	                                                    QueryMatcherDef::Glob(glob) => {
   203	                                                        L7QueryMatcher { glob, any: vec![] }
   204	                                                    }
   205	                                                    QueryMatcherDef::Any(any) => L7QueryMatcher {
   206	                                                        glob: String::new(),
   207	                                                        any: any.any,
   208	                                                    },
   209	                                                };
   210	                                                (key, proto)
   211	                                            })
   212	                                            .collect(),
   213	                                    }),
   214	                                })
   215	                                .collect(),
   216	                            allowed_ips: e.allowed_ips,
   217	                        }
   218	                    })
   219	                    .collect(),
   220	                binaries: rule
   221	                    .binaries
   222	                    .into_iter()
   223	                    .map(|b| NetworkBinary {
   224	                        path: b.path,
   225	                        ..Default::default()
   226	                    })
   227	                    .collect(),
   228	            };
   229	            (key, proto_rule)
   230	        })
   231	        .collect();
   232	
   233	    SandboxPolicy {
   234	        version: raw.version,
   235	        filesystem: raw.filesystem_policy.map(|fs| FilesystemPolicy {
   236	            include_workdir: fs.include_workdir,
   237	            read_only: fs.read_only,
   238	            read_write: fs.read_write,
   239	        }),
   240	        landlock: raw.landlock.map(|ll| LandlockPolicy {
   241	            compatibility: ll.compatibility,
   242	        }),
   243	        process: raw.process.map(|p| ProcessPolicy {
   244	            run_as_user: p.run_as_user,
   245	            run_as_group: p.run_as_group,
   246	        }),
   247	        network_policies,
   248	    }
   249	}
   250	
   251	// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   252	// Proto → YAML conversion
   253	// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   254	
   255	fn from_proto(policy: &SandboxPolicy) -> PolicyFile {
   256	    let filesystem_policy = policy.filesystem.as_ref().map(|fs| FilesystemDef {
   257	        include_workdir: fs.include_workdir,
   258	        read_only: fs.read_only.clone(),
   259	        read_write: fs.read_write.clone(),
   260	    });
   261	
   262	    let landlock = policy.landlock.as_ref().map(|ll| LandlockDef {
   263	        compatibility: ll.compatibility.clone(),
   264	    });
   265	
   266	    let process = policy.process.as_ref().and_then(|p| {
   267	        if p.run_as_user.is_empty() && p.run_as_group.is_empty() {
   268	            None
   269	        } else {
   270	            Some(ProcessDef {
   271	                run_as_user: p.run_as_user.clone(),
   272	                run_as_group: p.run_as_group.clone(),
   273	            })
   274	        }
   275	    });
   276	
   277	    let network_policies = policy
   278	        .network_policies
   279	        .iter()
   280	        .map(|(key, rule)| {
   281	            let yaml_rule = NetworkPolicyRuleDef {
   282	                name: rule.name.clone(),
   283	                endpoints: rule
   284	                    .endpoints
   285	                    .iter()
   286	                    .map(|e| {
   287	                        // Use compact form: if ports has exactly 1 element,
   288	                        // emit port (scalar). If >1, emit ports (array).
   289	                        // Proto uses u32; YAML uses u16. Clamp at boundary.
   290	                        let clamp = |v: u32| -> u16 { v.min(65535) as u16 };
   291	                        let (port, ports) = if e.ports.len() > 1 {
   292	                            (0, e.ports.iter().map(|&p| clamp(p)).collect())
   293	                        } else {
   294	                            (clamp(e.ports.first().copied().unwrap_or(e.port)), vec![])
   295	                        };
   296	                        NetworkEndpointDef {
   297	                            host: e.host.clone(),
   298	                            port,
   299	                            ports,
   300	                            protocol: e.protocol.clone(),
   301	                            tls: e.tls.clone(),
   302	                            enforcement: e.enforcement.clone(),
   303	                            access: e.access.clone(),
   304	                            rules: e
   305	                                .rules
   306	                                .iter()
   307	                                .map(|r| {
   308	                                    let a = r.allow.clone().unwrap_or_default();
   309	                                    L7RuleDef {
   310	                                        allow: L7AllowDef {
   311	                                            method: a.method,
   312	                                            path: a.path,
   313	                                            command: a.command,
   314	                                            query: a
   315	                                                .query
   316	                                                .into_iter()
   317	                                                .map(|(key, matcher)| {
   318	                                                    let yaml_matcher = if !matcher.any.is_empty() {
   319	                                                        QueryMatcherDef::Any(QueryAnyDef {
   320	                                                            any: matcher.any,
   321	                                                        })
   322	                                                    } else {
   323	                                                        QueryMatcherDef::Glob(matcher.glob)
   324	                                                    };
   325	                                                    (key, yaml_matcher)
   326	                                                })
   327	                                                .collect(),
   328	                                        },
   329	                                    }
   330	                                })
   331	                                .collect(),
   332	                            allowed_ips: e.allowed_ips.clone(),
   333	                        }
   334	                    })
   335	                    .collect(),
   336	                binaries: rule
   337	                    .binaries
   338	                    .iter()
   339	                    .map(|b| NetworkBinaryDef {
   340	                        path: b.path.clone(),
   341	                        harness: false,
   342	                    })
   343	                    .collect(),
   344	            };
   345	            (key.clone(), yaml_rule)
   346	        })
   347	        .collect();
   348	
   349	    PolicyFile {
   350	        version: policy.version,
   351	        filesystem_policy,
   352	        landlock,
   353	        process,
   354	        network_policies,
   355	    }
   356	}
   357	
   358	// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   359	// Public API
   360	// ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
   361	
   362	/// Parse a sandbox policy from a YAML string.
   363	pub fn parse_sandbox_policy(yaml: &str) -> Result<SandboxPolicy> {
   364	    let raw: PolicyFile = serde_yml::from_str(yaml)
   365	        .into_diagnostic()
   366	        .wrap_err("failed to parse sandbox policy YAML")?;
   367	    Ok(to_proto(raw))
   368	}
   369	
   370	/// Serialize a proto sandbox policy to a YAML string.
   371	///
   372	/// This is the inverse of [`parse_sandbox_policy`] — the output uses the
   373	/// canonical YAML field names (e.g. `filesystem_policy`, not `filesystem`)
   374	/// and is round-trippable through `parse_sandbox_policy`.
   375	pub fn serialize_sandbox_policy(policy: &SandboxPolicy) -> Result<String> {
   376	    let yaml_repr = from_proto(policy);
   377	    serde_yml::to_string(&yaml_repr)
   378	        .into_diagnostic()
   379	        .wrap_err("failed to serialize policy to YAML")
   380	}
   381	
   382	/// Load a sandbox policy from an explicit source.
   383	///
   384	/// Resolution order:
   385	/// 1. `cli_path` argument (e.g. from a `--policy` flag)
   386	/// 2. `OPENSHELL_SANDBOX_POLICY` environment variable
   387	///
   388	/// Returns `Ok(None)` when no policy source is configured, allowing the
   389	/// caller to omit the policy and let the server / sandbox apply its own
   390	/// default.
   391	pub fn load_sandbox_policy(cli_path: Option<&str>) -> Result<Option<SandboxPolicy>> {
   392	    let contents = if let Some(p) = cli_path {
   393	        let path = Path::new(p);
   394	        std::fs::read_to_string(path)
   395	            .into_diagnostic()
   396	            .wrap_err_with(|| format!("failed to read sandbox policy from {}", path.display()))?
   397	    } else if let Ok(policy_path) = std::env::var("OPENSHELL_SANDBOX_POLICY") {
   398	        let path = Path::new(&policy_path);
   399	        std::fs::read_to_string(path)
   400	            .into_diagnostic()
   401	            .wrap_err_with(|| format!("failed to read sandbox policy from {}", path.display()))?
   402	    } else {
   403	        return Ok(None);
   404	    };
   405	    parse_sandbox_policy(&contents).map(Some)
   406	}

     4	//! Sandbox policy configuration.
     5	
     6	use openshell_core::proto::{
     7	    FilesystemPolicy as ProtoFilesystemPolicy, LandlockPolicy as ProtoLandlockPolicy,
     8	    ProcessPolicy as ProtoProcessPolicy, SandboxPolicy as ProtoSandboxPolicy,
     9	};
    10	use std::net::SocketAddr;
    11	use std::path::PathBuf;
    12	
    13	#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
    14	pub struct SandboxPolicy {
    15	    pub version: u32,
    16	    pub filesystem: FilesystemPolicy,
    17	    pub network: NetworkPolicy,
    18	    pub landlock: LandlockPolicy,
    19	    pub process: ProcessPolicy,
    20	}
    21	
    22	#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
    23	pub struct FilesystemPolicy {
    24	    /// Read-only directory allow list.
    25	    pub read_only: Vec<PathBuf>,
    26	
    27	    /// Read-write directory allow list.
    28	    pub read_write: Vec<PathBuf>,
    29	
    30	    /// Automatically include the workdir as read-write.
    31	    pub include_workdir: bool,
    32	}
    33	
    34	impl Default for FilesystemPolicy {
    35	    fn default() -> Self {
    36	        Self {
    37	            read_only: Vec::new(),
    38	            read_write: Vec::new(),
    39	            include_workdir: true,
    40	        }
    41	    }
    42	}
    43	
    44	#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
    45	pub struct NetworkPolicy {
    46	    pub mode: NetworkMode,
    47	    pub proxy: Option<ProxyPolicy>,
    48	}
    49	
    50	impl Default for NetworkPolicy {
    51	    fn default() -> Self {
    52	        Self {
    53	            mode: NetworkMode::Block,
    54	            proxy: None,
    55	        }
    56	    }
    57	}
    58	
    59	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default)]
    60	pub enum NetworkMode {
    61	    #[default]
    62	    Block,
    63	    Proxy,
    64	    Allow,
    65	}
    66	
    67	#[derive(Debug, Clone)]
    68	pub struct ProxyPolicy {
    69	    /// TCP address for a local HTTP proxy (loopback-only).
    70	    pub http_addr: Option<SocketAddr>,
    71	}
    72	
    73	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default)]
    74	pub struct LandlockPolicy {
    75	    pub compatibility: LandlockCompatibility,
    76	}
    77	
    78	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default)]
    79	pub struct ProcessPolicy {
    80	    /// User name to run the sandboxed process as.
    81	    pub run_as_user: Option<String>,
    82	
    83	    /// Group name to run the sandboxed process as.
    84	    pub run_as_group: Option<String>,
    85	}
    86	
    87	#[derive(Debug, Clone, Default)]
    88	pub enum LandlockCompatibility {
    89	    #[default]
    90	    BestEffort,
    91	    HardRequirement,
    92	}
    93	
    94	// ============================================================================
    95	// Proto to Rust type conversions
    96	// ============================================================================
    97	
    98	impl TryFrom<ProtoSandboxPolicy> for SandboxPolicy {
    99	    type Error = miette::Report;
   100	
   101	    fn try_from(proto: ProtoSandboxPolicy) -> Result<Self, Self::Error> {
   102	        // In cluster mode we always run with proxy networking so all egress
   103	        // can be evaluated by OPA and `inference.local` is always addressable.
   104	        let network = NetworkPolicy {
   105	            mode: NetworkMode::Proxy,
   106	            proxy: Some(ProxyPolicy { http_addr: None }),
   107	        };
   108	
   109	        Ok(Self {
   110	            version: proto.version,
   111	            filesystem: proto
   112	                .filesystem
   113	                .map(FilesystemPolicy::from)
   114	                .unwrap_or_default(),
   115	            network,
   116	            landlock: proto.landlock.map(LandlockPolicy::from).unwrap_or_default(),
   117	            process: proto.process.map(ProcessPolicy::from).unwrap_or_default(),
   118	        })
   119	    }
   120	}
   121	
   122	impl From<ProtoFilesystemPolicy> for FilesystemPolicy {
   123	    fn from(proto: ProtoFilesystemPolicy) -> Self {
   124	        Self {
   125	            read_only: proto
   126	                .read_only
   127	                .into_iter()
   128	                .map(|p| PathBuf::from(openshell_policy::normalize_path(&p)))
   129	                .collect(),
   130	            read_write: proto
   131	                .read_write
   132	                .into_iter()
   133	                .map(|p| PathBuf::from(openshell_policy::normalize_path(&p)))
   134	                .collect(),
   135	            include_workdir: proto.include_workdir,
   136	        }
   137	    }
   138	}
   139	
   140	impl From<ProtoLandlockPolicy> for LandlockPolicy {
   141	    fn from(proto: ProtoLandlockPolicy) -> Self {
   142	        let compatibility = if proto.compatibility == "hard_requirement" {
   143	            LandlockCompatibility::HardRequirement
   144	        } else {
   145	            LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort
   146	        };
   147	        Self { compatibility }
   148	    }
   149	}
   150	
   151	impl From<ProtoProcessPolicy> for ProcessPolicy {
   152	    fn from(proto: ProtoProcessPolicy) -> Self {
   153	        Self {
   154	            run_as_user: if proto.run_as_user.is_empty() {
   155	                None
   156	            } else {
   157	                Some(proto.run_as_user)
   158	            },
   159	            run_as_group: if proto.run_as_group.is_empty() {
   160	                None
   161	            } else {
   162	                Some(proto.run_as_group)
   163	            },
   164	        }
   165	    }
   166	}
   167

2026-06-01 05:08:03,611 - INFO - swea-agent-NVIDIA__OpenShell-810 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I have a thorough understanding of the problem. Let me summarize the issue and the fix:

**The Problem:**
1. In `process.rs`, `drop_privileges()` is called BEFORE `sandbox::apply()` (line 184-187). This switches from root to sandbox user.
2. Then `landlock::apply()` tries to open paths using `PathFd::new(path)` which calls `open(path, O_PATH | O_CLOEXEC)` as the unprivileged sandbox user.
3. If any path fails to open (e.g., permission denied), and we're in `BestEffort` mode, the error is silently swallowed and `Ok(())` is returned — Landlock is never applied.
4. Even if `restrict_self()` fails (e.g., because `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` isn't set), the error is also swallowed.

**The Fix (as described in the PR):**
We need a two-phase approach:
1. Phase 1 (as root): Open path FDs + create ruleset BEFORE `drop_privileges()`
2. Phase 2 (after `drop_privileges()`): Call `restrict_self()` only

Let me look at more of the landlock API to understand how to split the operation

The key insight from the docs is that `RulesetCreated::restrict_self()` takes `self` (consumes the ruleset). So we need to:

1. Create the ruleset (open FDs, build rules) as root
2. Then restrict_self after dropping privileges

But `restrict_self()` consumes the `RulesetCreated`. However, looking at the landlock crate, `RulesetCreated` has a `try_clone()` method! That's the key.

Let me look more at the crate source

2026-06-01 05:09:05,754 - INFO - swea-agent-NVIDIA__OpenShell-810 - 💭 THOUGHT
`RulesetCreated` has `try_clone()`. So the approach is:

1. Before `drop_privileges()`, open paths, create the ruleset, add rules (all as root)
2. After `drop_privileges()`, call `restrict_self()` on the ruleset

Now let me look at how `process.rs` calls the sandbox and how we can restructure this. The key challenge is that `sandbox::apply()` is called inside `pre_exec`, which is a closure that runs after fork. The FD approach should work because we can open FDs before the fork and pass them through.

Let me reconsider the architecture:

Looking at `process.rs`:
- Line 166-192: `pre_exec` closure that runs in the child process after fork
- Line 184: `drop_privileges(&policy)`
- Line 187: `sandbox::apply(&policy, workdir.as_deref())`

The `pre_exec` closure runs in the child process after `fork()`. At this point we can still be root (before `drop_privileges`). The issue is that the Landlock operations (opening paths, creating rulesets) happen AFTER `drop_privileges`.

The fix should restructure `landlock::apply()` to split into two phases:
1. A "build" phase that opens FDs and creates the ruleset (must be done as root)
2. A "restrict" phase that calls `restrict_self()` (can be done after dropping privileges)

But since `RulesetCreated::try_clone()` exists, we can:
1. Build the ruleset with all FDs opened as root
2. Clone it (or just keep it) 
3. Drop privileges
4. Call `restrict_self()` on the cloned ruleset

Actually, looking more carefully at the landlock source code, `restrict_self()` consumes `self`, but `try_clone()` duplicates the fd. So we can clone before dropping privileges and use the clone for `restrict_self()` after.

But wait - there's a simpler approach: just reorder the operations in `process.rs` to call `sandbox::apply()` BEFORE `drop_privileges()`, and make the landlock code handle both phases correctly.

Let me look at the landlock crate source more carefully to understand what `restrict_self()` does:

The landlock syscalls are:
1. `landlock_create_ruleset` - creates a ruleset fd
2. `landlock_add_rule` - adds rules to the ruleset fd
3. `landlock_restrict_self` - enforces the ruleset

All three syscalls require `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` to be set. The `landlock` crate likely handles this.

Now, the critical insight is: the `RulesetCreated` struct holds a file descriptor (the ruleset fd). `try_clone()` duplicates this fd. `restrict_self()` consumes the `RulesetCreated` and calls `landlock_restrict_self()`.

The plan:
1. In `landlock::apply()`, split into `build_ruleset()` and `restrict_self()` phases
2. In `process.rs`, call sandbox apply BEFORE dropping privileges but only do the build phase, then drop privileges, then do the restrict phase

Actually, a cleaner approach: modify the `landlock::apply()` to accept a parameter indicating whether to do the full apply or just build+return the ruleset. But that changes the API.

Even cleaner: Since `RulesetCreated` implements `Send` and has `try_clone()`, we can:
1. Build the ruleset (as root) - open FDs, create ruleset, add rules
2. Store the `RulesetCreated`
3. Drop privileges
4. Call `restrict_self()` on the stored ruleset

But the problem is that this is all in `pre_exec` which runs after fork. At that point we ARE still root until we call `drop_privileges`. So we just need to reorder: call sandbox::apply BEFORE drop_privileges.

Wait, let me re-read the pre_exec code:

```rust
cmd.pre_exec(move || {
    // ...
    // Drop privileges before applying sandbox restrictions.
    drop_privileges(&policy)?;
    sandbox::apply(&policy, workdir.as_deref())?;
    Ok(())
});
```

The fix is simple: swap the order of these two calls! Call `sandbox::apply()` first (which opens FDs and creates the ruleset as root), then call `drop_privileges()` (which switches to sandbox user), then call `restrict_self()` (which enforces the ruleset).

But that requires `sandbox::apply` to be split into two phases: build (as root) and enforce (can be as any user).

Let me now implement this. The approach:

1. Modify `landlock.rs` to export two functions: `build_ruleset()` and `restrict_self(ruleset)`.
2. Modify `process.rs` to call build before drop_privileges and restrict after.

Actually, looking at this more carefully, let me look at how the `landlock` crate works internally. The `RulesetCreated` has `try_clone()`. So we can:

1. Build the ruleset (open FDs, create, add rules) → returns `RulesetCreated`
2. Clone it before or after drop_privileges 
3. Call `restrict_self()` on the clone

But wait, the issue in the PR description says `restrict_self()` requires `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS`. Does the landlock crate set this? Let me check...

Looking at the landlock crate doc: `RulesetCreated::restrict_self()` documentation says it calls `landlock_restrict_self()`. The `RulesetCreatedAttr` trait has `set_no_new_privs()` method. But the current code doesn't call `set_no_new_privs()` explicitly. Let me check if the landlock crate auto-sets it...

Actually, looking at the landlock crate source (via the docs), I see:
- `RulesetCreatedAttr::set_no_new_privs()` sets `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS`
- `restrict_self()` likely calls `set_no_new_privs` internally or requires it

Let me check what the current code does:

```rust
let mut ruleset = ruleset.create().into_diagnostic()?;
// ... add rules ...
ruleset.restrict_self().into_diagnostic()?;
```

The `restrict_self()` method on `RulesetCreated` should handle `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` internally. Let me verify by checking the landlock crate source...

--
<a href=#756 id=756 data-nosnippet>756</a>    </span><span class="kw">pub fn </span>restrict_self(<span class="kw-2">mut </span><span class="self">self</span>) -&gt; <span class="prelude-ty">Result</span>&lt;RestrictionStatus, RulesetError&gt; {
<a href=#757 id=757 data-nosnippet>757</a>        <span class="kw">let </span><span class="kw-2">mut </span>body = || -&gt; <span class="prelude-ty">Result</span>&lt;RestrictionStatus, RestrictSelfError&gt; {
<a href=#758 id=758 data-nosnippet>758</a>            <span class="comment">// Enforce no_new_privs even if something failed with SoftRequirement. The rationale is
<a href=#759 id=759 data-nosnippet>759</a>            // that no_new_privs should not be an issue on its own if it is not explicitly
<a href=#760 id=760 data-nosnippet>760</a>            // deactivated.
<a href=#761 id=761 data-nosnippet>761</a>            </span><span class="kw">let </span>enforced_nnp = <span class="kw">if </span><span class="self">self</span>.no_new_privs {
<a href=#762 id=762 data-nosnippet>762</a>                <span class="kw">if let </span><span class="prelude-val">Err</span>(e) = prctl_set_no_new_privs() {
<a href=#763 id=763 data-nosnippet>763</a>                    <span class="kw">match </span><span class="self">self</span>.compat.level.into() {
<a href=#764 id=764 data-nosnippet>764</a>                        CompatLevel::BestEffort =&gt; {}
<a href=#765 id=765 data-nosnippet>765</a>                        CompatLevel::SoftRequirement =&gt; {
<a href=#766 id=766 data-nosnippet>766</a>                            <span class="self">self</span>.compat.update(CompatState::Dummy);
<a href=#767 id=767 data-nosnippet>767</a>                        }
<a href=#768 id=768 data-nosnippet>768</a>                        CompatLevel::HardRequirement =&gt; {
<a href=#769 id=769 data-nosnippet>769</a>                            <span class="kw">return </span><span class="prelude-val">Err</span>(RestrictSelfError::SetNoNewPrivsCall { source: e });
<a href=#770 id=770 data-nosnippet>770</a>                        }
<a href=#771 id=771 data-nosnippet>771</a>                    }
<a href=#772 id=772 data-nosnippet>772</a>                    <span class="comment">// To get a consistent behavior, calls this prctl whether or not
<a href=#773 id=773 data-nosnippet>773</a>                    // Landlock is supported by the running kernel.
<a href=#774 id=774 data-nosnippet>774</a>                    </span><span class="kw">let </span>support_nnp = support_no_new_privs();
<a href=#775 id=775 data-nosnippet>775</a>                    <span class="kw">match </span><span class="self">self</span>.compat.state {
<a href=#776 id=776 data-nosnippet>776</a>                        <span class="comment">// It should not be an error for kernel (older than 3.5) not supporting
<a href=#777 id=777 data-nosnippet>777</a>                        // no_new_privs.
<a href=#778 id=778 data-nosnippet>778</a>                        </span>CompatState::Init | CompatState::No | CompatState::Dummy =&gt; {
<a href=#779 id=779 data-nosnippet>779</a>                            <span class="kw">if </span>support_nnp {
<a href=#780 id=780 data-nosnippet>780</a>                                <span class="comment">// The kernel seems to be between 3.5 (included) and 5.13 (excluded),
<a href=#781 id=781 data-nosnippet>781</a>                                // or Landlock is not enabled; no_new_privs should be supported anyway.
<a href=#782 id=782 data-nosnippet>782</a>                                </span><span class="kw">return </span><span class="prelude-val">Err</span>(RestrictSelfError::SetNoNewPrivsCall { source: e });
<a href=#783 id=783 data-nosnippet>783</a>                            }
<a href=#784 id=784 data-nosnippet>784</a>                        }
<a href=#785 id=785 data-nosnippet>785</a>                        <span class="comment">// A kernel supporting Landlock should also support no_new_privs (unless
<a href=#786 id=786 data-nosnippet>786</a>                        // filtered by seccomp).
--
<a href=#810 id=810 data-nosnippet>810</a>                    <span class="kw">match unsafe </span>{ uapi::landlock_restrict_self(fd, <span class="number">0</span>) } {
<a href=#811 id=811 data-nosnippet>811</a>                        <span class="number">0 </span>=&gt; {
<a href=#812 id=812 data-nosnippet>812</a>                            <span class="self">self</span>.compat.update(CompatState::Full);
<a href=#813 id=813 data-nosnippet>813</a>                            <span class="prelude-val">Ok</span>(RestrictionStatus {
<a href=#814 id=814 data-nosnippet>814</a>                                ruleset: <span class="self">self</span>.compat.state.into(),
<a href=#815 id=815 data-nosnippet>815</a>                                landlock: <span class="self">self</span>.compat.status(),
<a href=#816 id=816 data-nosnippet>816</a>                                no_new_privs: enforced_nnp,
<a href=#817 id=817 data-nosnippet>817</a>                            })
<a href=#818 id=818 data-nosnippet>818</a>                        }
<a href=#819 id=819 data-nosnippet>819</a>                        <span class="comment">// TODO: match specific Landlock restrict self errors
<a href=#820 id=820 data-nosnippet>820</a>                        </span><span class="kw">_ </span>=&gt; <span class="prelude-val">Err</span>(RestrictSelfError::RestrictSelfCall {
<a href=#821 id=821 data-nosnippet>821</a>                            source: Error::last_os_error(),
<a href=#822 id=822 data-nosnippet>822</a>                        }),
<a href=#823 id=823 data-nosnippet>823</a>                    }
<a href=#824 id=824 data-nosnippet>824</a>                }
<a href=#825 id=825 data-nosnippet>825</a>            }
<a href=#826 id=826 data-nosnippet>826</a>        };
<a href=#827 id=827 data-nosnippet>827</a>        <span class="prelude-val">Ok</span>(body()<span class="question-mark">?</span>)
<a href=#828 id=828 data-nosnippet>828</a>    }
<a href=#829 id=829 data-nosnippet>829</a>
<a href=#830 id=830 data-nosnippet>830</a>    <span class="doccomment">/// Creates a new `RulesetCreated` instance by duplicating the underlying file descriptor.
<a href=#831 id=831 data-nosnippet>831</a>    /// Rule modification will affect both `RulesetCreated` instances simultaneously.
<a href=#832 id=832 data-nosnippet>832</a>    ///
<a href=#833 id=833 data-nosnippet>833</a>    /// On error, returns [`std::io::Error`].
<a href=#834 id=834 data-nosnippet>834</a>    </span><span class="kw">pub fn </span>try_clone(<span class="kw-2">&amp;</span><span class="self">self</span>) -&gt; std::io::Result&lt;<span class="self">Self</span>&gt; {
<a href=#835 id=835 data-nosnippet>835</a>        <span class="prelude-val">Ok</span>(RulesetCreated {
<a href=#836 id=836 data-nosnippet>836</a>            fd: <span class="self">self</span>.fd.as_ref().map(|f| f.try_clone()).transpose()<span class="question-mark">?</span>,
<a href=#837 id=837 data-nosnippet>837</a>            no_new_privs: <span class="self">self</span>.no_new_privs,
<a href=#838 id=838 data-nosnippet>838</a>            requested_handled_fs: <span class="self">self</span>.requested_handled_fs,
<a href=#839 id=839 data-nosnippet>839</a>            requested_handled_net: <span class="self">self</span>.requested_handled_net,
<a href=#840 id=840 data-nosnippet>840</a>            compat: <span class="self">self</span>.compat,
--
<a href=#909 id=909 data-nosnippet>909</a>            .restrict_self()
<a href=#910 id=910 data-nosnippet>910</a>            .unwrap(),
<a href=#911 id=911 data-nosnippet>911</a>        RestrictionStatus {
<a href=#912 id=912 data-nosnippet>912</a>            ruleset: RulesetStatus::NotEnforced,
<a href=#913 id=913 data-nosnippet>913</a>            landlock: LandlockStatus::NotImplemented,
<a href=#914 id=914 data-nosnippet>914</a>            no_new_privs: <span class="bool-val">true</span>,
<a href=#915 id=915 data-nosnippet>915</a>        }
<a href=#916 id=916 data-nosnippet>916</a>    );
<a href=#917 id=917 data-nosnippet>917</a>}
