2026-06-01 05:10:25,366 - INFO - swea-agent-NVIDIA__OpenShell-810 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I have a clear picture. From the landlock crate source:

1. `restrict_self()` sets `no_new_privs` by default (line 742: `no_new_privs: true`)
2. `restrict_self()` calls `prctl_set_no_new_privs()` internally
3. `RulesetCreated` has `try_clone()` which duplicates the fd

So the approach is:
1. In `landlock.rs`, split `apply()` into two functions:
   - `build_ruleset()` - opens FDs, creates ruleset, adds rules → returns `RulesetCreated`
   - Call `restrict_self()` on the ruleset

2. In `process.rs`, reorder:
   - Call `sandbox::apply_build()` (or similar) BEFORE `drop_privileges()`
   - Drop privileges
   - Call `restrict_self()` on the built ruleset

But this creates a problem: `RulesetCreated` is not `Send` across the `pre_exec` boundary cleanly (it IS `Send` based on the docs). Actually, it is `Send` based on the auto trait implementations.

Wait, let me step back. The `pre_exec` closure runs in the child process after fork. At that point, we have the same memory as the parent. The `pre_exec` closure is `move`, so it captures everything by value. The closure runs before `exec()`.

So the flow in `pre_exec` is:
1. We are in the child process
2. We are still root (unless the parent was not root)
3. `drop_privileges()` switches to sandbox user
4. `sandbox::apply()` tries to enforce Landlock

The fix is to reorder: apply sandbox BEFORE dropping privileges. But we also need `restrict_self()` to happen (it can happen after drop_privileges, since it just needs the fd).

Let me think about the cleanest way to do this:

**Option A**: Split landlock::apply into two functions:
- `prepare_ruleset()` → returns `RulesetCreated` 
- Then caller does `ruleset.restrict_self()`

Modify `process.rs`:
1. Call `prepare_ruleset()` (as root) 
2. `drop_privileges()`
3. `ruleset.restrict_self()`

**Option B**: Just reorder in `process.rs` to call `sandbox::apply()` before `drop_privileges()`.

Option B is simpler but doesn't address the `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` concern. Let me check: does the landlock crate's `restrict_self()` set `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS`? Yes, it does by default (line 742 sets `no_new_privs: true`).

So if we call `sandbox::apply()` (which internally calls `restrict_self()`) BEFORE `drop_privileges()`, then `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` is set as root, and then we try to `setuid()` in `drop_privileges()`. But `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` prevents `setuid` from gaining new privileges - it doesn't prevent dropping privileges (setuid to a non-root user). Actually, `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` only prevents gaining new privileges, not dropping them. So this should be fine.

Wait, actually there's a nuance. The `landlock_restrict_self()` syscall enforces the ruleset for the current thread. Once enforced, it cannot be removed. If we apply Landlock before dropping privileges, the Landlock policy will apply to root, and then we drop to sandbox user. The Landlock restrictions follow the process even after setuid. That should be fine.

But actually the current comment in process.rs says:
```
// Drop privileges before applying sandbox restrictions.
// initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
// which may be blocked by Landlock.
```

This is important! If Landlock blocks access to `/etc/group` and `/etc/passwd`, then `initgroups/setgid/setuid` would fail. So the current order (drop first, then apply Landlock) is intentional to allow these files to be accessed.

But the problem is that after dropping privileges, we can't open the paths we need for Landlock rules.

The correct solution (as described in the PR) is the two-phase approach:
1. Phase 1 (as root): Open path FDs + create ruleset (don't call restrict_self yet)
2. Phase 2 (after drop_privileges): Call restrict_self() to enforce

This way:
- `/etc/passwd` and `/etc/group` are still accessible when we need them for `drop_privileges()`
- We open the Landlock paths as root (before dropping privileges)
- We enforce Landlock after dropping privileges (so the sandbox user is restricted)

Let me now implement this.

First, let me check whether `RulesetCreated` can cross the closure boundary. It's `Send` and not `Sync`, but we're in a single-threaded context, so it's fine.

Let me modify `landlock.rs` to split into two functions

🎬 ACTION

// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0

//! Landlock filesystem sandboxing.

use crate::policy::{LandlockCompatibility, SandboxPolicy};
use landlock::{
    ABI, Access, AccessFs, CompatLevel, Compatible, PathBeneath, PathFd, PathFdError, Ruleset,
    RulesetAttr, RulesetCreatedAttr,
};
use miette::{IntoDiagnostic, Result};
use std::path::{Path, PathBuf};
use tracing::debug;

pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    let read_only = policy.filesystem.read_only.clone();
    let mut read_write = policy.filesystem.read_write.clone();

    if policy.filesystem.include_workdir
        && let Some(dir) = workdir
    {
        let workdir_path = PathBuf::from(dir);
        if !read_write.contains(&workdir_path) {
            read_write.push(workdir_path);
        }
    }

    if read_only.is_empty() && read_write.is_empty() {
        return Ok(());
    }

    let total_paths = read_only.len() + read_write.len();
    let abi = ABI::V2;
    openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
        openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
            .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
            .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
            .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "applying")
            .message(format!(
                "Applying Landlock filesystem sandbox [abi:{abi:?} compat:{:?} ro:{} rw:{}]",
                policy.landlock.compatibility,
                read_only.len(),
                read_write.len(),
            ))
            .build()
    );

    let compatibility = &policy.landlock.compatibility;

    let result: Result<()> = (|| {
        let access_all = AccessFs::from_all(abi);
        let access_read = AccessFs::from_read(abi);

        let mut ruleset = Ruleset::default();
        ruleset = ruleset
            .set_compatibility(compat_level(compatibility))
            .handle_access(access_all)
            .into_diagnostic()?;

        let mut ruleset = ruleset.create().into_diagnostic()?;
        let mut rules_applied: usize = 0;

        for path in &read_only {
            if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, compatibility)? {
                debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-only");
                ruleset = ruleset
                    .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_read))
                    .into_diagnostic()?;
                rules_applied += 1;
            }
        }

        for path in &read_write {
            if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, compatibility)? {
                debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-write");
                ruleset = ruleset
                    .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_all))
                    .into_diagnostic()?;
                rules_applied += 1;
            }
        }

        if rules_applied == 0 {
            return Err(miette::miette!(
                "Landlock ruleset has zero valid paths — all {} path(s) failed to open. \
                 Refusing to apply an empty ruleset that would block all filesystem access.",
                total_paths,
            ));
        }

        let skipped = total_paths - rules_applied;
        openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
            openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
                .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
                .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "built")
                .message(format!(
                    "Landlock ruleset built [rules_applied:{rules_applied} skipped:{skipped}]"
                ))
                .build()
        );

        ruleset.restrict_self().into_diagnostic()?;
        Ok(())
    })();

    if let Err(err) = result {
        if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
            openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
                openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                    .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
                    .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
                    .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
                    .is_alert(true)
                    .finding_info(
                        openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
                            "landlock-unavailable",
                            "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
                        )
                        .with_desc(&format!(
                            "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
                             Set landlock.compatibility to '"'"'hard_requirement'"'"' to make this fatal."
                        )),
                    )
                    .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
                    .build()
            );
            return Ok(());
        }
        return Err(err);
    }

    Ok(())

// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0

//! Landlock filesystem sandboxing.

use crate::policy::{LandlockCompatibility, SandboxPolicy};
use landlock::{
    ABI, Access, AccessFs, CompatLevel, Compatible, PathBeneath, PathFd, PathFdError, Ruleset,
    RulesetAttr, RulesetCreated, RulesetCreatedAttr,
};
use miette::{IntoDiagnostic, Result};
use std::path::{Path, PathBuf};
use tracing::debug;

/// Build a Landlock ruleset by opening path FDs and creating the ruleset.
///
/// This phase requires the caller to have privileges to open the paths
/// (i.e., run as root). It returns the built ruleset which can later
/// be enforced via [`restrict`].
pub fn build_ruleset(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<RulesetCreated> {
    let read_only = policy.filesystem.read_only.clone();
    let mut read_write = policy.filesystem.read_write.clone();

    if policy.filesystem.include_workdir
        && let Some(dir) = workdir
    {
        let workdir_path = PathBuf::from(dir);
        if !read_write.contains(&workdir_path) {
            read_write.push(workdir_path);
        }
    }

    if read_only.is_empty() && read_write.is_empty() {
        // Return an empty ruleset marker. Callers can detect this case.
        return Err(miette::miette!("No filesystem paths configured for Landlock"));
    }

    let total_paths = read_only.len() + read_write.len();
    let abi = ABI::V2;
    openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
        openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
            .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
            .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
            .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "building")
            .message(format!(
                "Building Landlock filesystem ruleset [abi:{abi:?} compat:{:?} ro:{} rw:{}]",
                policy.landlock.compatibility,
                read_only.len(),
                read_write.len(),
            ))
            .build()
    );

    let compatibility = &policy.landlock.compatibility;

    let access_all = AccessFs::from_all(abi);
    let access_read = AccessFs::from_read(abi);

    let mut ruleset = Ruleset::default();
    ruleset = ruleset
        .set_compatibility(compat_level(compatibility))
        .handle_access(access_all)
        .into_diagnostic()?;

    let mut ruleset = ruleset.create().into_diagnostic()?;
    let mut rules_applied: usize = 0;

    for path in &read_only {
        if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, compatibility)? {
            debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-only");
            ruleset = ruleset
                .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_read))
                .into_diagnostic()?;
            rules_applied += 1;
        }
    }

    for path in &read_write {
        if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, compatibility)? {
            debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-write");
            ruleset = ruleset
                .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_all))
                .into_diagnostic()?;
            rules_applied += 1;
        }
    }

    if rules_applied == 0 {
        return Err(miette::miette!(
            "Landlock ruleset has zero valid paths — all {} path(s) failed to open. \
             Refusing to apply an empty ruleset that would block all filesystem access.",
            total_paths,
        ));
    }

    let skipped = total_paths - rules_applied;
    openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
        openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
            .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
            .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
            .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "built")
            .message(format!(
                "Landlock ruleset built [rules_applied:{rules_applied} skipped:{skipped}]"
            ))
            .build()
    );

    Ok(ruleset)
}

/// Enforce a previously-built Landlock ruleset via `restrict_self()`.
///
/// This phase may be called after dropping privileges, since it only
/// requires the ruleset file descriptor (already created) and
/// `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` (which is set internally by the landlock crate).
pub fn restrict(
    ruleset: RulesetCreated,
    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
) -> Result<()> {
    let result: Result<()> = (|| {
        ruleset.restrict_self().into_diagnostic()?;
        Ok(())
    })();

    if let Err(err) = result {
        if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
            openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
                openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                    .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
                    .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
                    .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
                    .is_alert(true)
                    .finding_info(
                        openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
                            "landlock-unavailable",
                            "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
                        )
                        .with_desc(&format!(
                            "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
                             Set landlock.compatibility to '"'"'hard_requirement'"'"' to make this fatal."
                        )),
                    )
                    .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
                    .build()
            );
            return Ok(());
        }
        return Err(err);
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Apply Landlock filesystem sandboxing (build + restrict in one step).
///
/// This is the legacy entry point used when the caller already has the
/// appropriate privileges and wants to build and enforce in one call.
/// Prefer [`build_ruleset`] + [`restrict`] for better control over which
/// phase runs with which privileges.
pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
    match build_ruleset(policy, workdir) {
        Ok(ruleset) => restrict(ruleset, &compatibility),
        Err(err) => {
            if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
                openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
                    openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                        .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
                        .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
                        .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
                        .is_alert(true)
                        .finding_info(
                            openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
                                "landlock-unavailable",
                                "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
                            )
                            .with_desc(&format!(
                                "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
                                 Set landlock.compatibility to '"'"'hard_requirement'"'"' to make this fatal."
                            )),
                        )
                        .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
                        .build()
                );
                Ok(())
            } else {
                Err(err)
            }
        }
    }
}'

//! Linux sandbox implementation using Landlock and seccomp.

//! Linux sandbox implementation using Landlock and seccomp.

mod landlock;
pub mod netns;
mod seccomp;

use crate::policy::{LandlockCompatibility, SandboxPolicy};
use landlock::RulesetCreated;
use miette::Result;

/// Build Landlock ruleset (requires privileges to open paths).
/// Returns the built ruleset for later enforcement.
pub fn build_landlock_ruleset(
    policy: &SandboxPolicy,
    workdir: Option<&str>,
) -> Result<RulesetCreated> {
    landlock::build_ruleset(policy, workdir)
}

/// Enforce a previously-built Landlock ruleset.
pub fn restrict_landlock(
    ruleset: RulesetCreated,
    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
) -> Result<()> {
    landlock::restrict(ruleset, compatibility)
}

/// Apply sandboxing rules for the current platform (one-shot).
pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    landlock::apply(policy, workdir)?;
    seccomp::apply(policy)?;
    Ok(())
}

/// Apply seccomp only (used after two-phase Landlock).
pub fn apply_seccomp(policy: &SandboxPolicy) -> Result<()> {
    seccomp::apply(policy)

// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0

//! Platform sandboxing implementation.

use crate::policy::{LandlockCompatibility, SandboxPolicy};
use miette::Result;

#[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
pub mod linux;

/// Opaque handle to a built (but not yet enforced) Landlock ruleset.
///
/// On Linux this wraps the landlock crate'"'"'s `RulesetCreated`.
/// On other platforms this is a unit struct.
#[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
pub type LandlockRulesetHandle = linux::LandlockRulesetHandle;

#[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
pub struct LandlockRulesetHandle;

/// Build a Landlock ruleset (requires privileges to open paths).
///
/// This opens path FDs and creates the Landlock ruleset, but does NOT
/// call `restrict_self()` yet. The returned handle can be used with
/// [`restrict_landlock`] to enforce the ruleset after privileges have
/// been dropped.
///
/// # Errors
///
/// Returns an error if the ruleset cannot be built.
#[cfg_attr(not(target_os = "linux"), allow(clippy::unnecessary_wraps))]
pub fn build_landlock_ruleset(
    policy: &SandboxPolicy,
    workdir: Option<&str>,
) -> Result<Option<LandlockRulesetHandle>> {
    #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
    {
        linux::build_landlock_ruleset(policy, workdir).map(Some)
    }

    #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
    {
        let _ = (policy, workdir);
        Ok(None)
    }
}

/// Enforce a previously-built Landlock ruleset.
///
/// This calls `restrict_self()` on the ruleset. It can be called after
/// privileges have been dropped.
///
/// # Errors
///
/// Returns an error if the ruleset cannot be enforced.
#[cfg_attr(not(target_os = "linux"), allow(clippy::unnecessary_wraps))]
pub fn restrict_landlock(
    handle: LandlockRulesetHandle,
    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
) -> Result<()> {
    #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
    {
        linux::restrict_landlock(handle, compatibility)
    }

    #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
    {
        let _ = (handle, compatibility);
        Ok(())
    }
}

/// Apply sandboxing rules for the current platform (one-shot).
///
/// # Errors
///
/// Returns an error if the sandbox cannot be applied.
#[cfg_attr(not(target_os = "linux"), allow(clippy::unnecessary_wraps))]
pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
    {
        linux::apply(policy, workdir)
    }

    #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
    {
        let _ = (policy, workdir);
        openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
            openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
                .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Medium)
                .finding_info(openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
                    "platform-sandbox-unavailable",
                    "Platform Sandboxing Not Implemented",
                ).with_desc("Sandbox policy provided but platform sandboxing is not yet implemented on this OS"))
                .message("Platform sandboxing not yet implemented")
                .build()
        );
        Ok(())
    }
}

/// Apply seccomp only (used after two-phase Landlock on Linux).
///
/// # Errors
///
/// Returns an error if seccomp cannot be applied.
#[cfg_attr(not(target_os = "linux"), allow(clippy::unnecessary_wraps))]
pub fn apply_seccomp(policy: &SandboxPolicy) -> Result<()> {
    #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
    {
        linux::apply_seccomp(policy)
    }

    #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
    {
        let _ = policy;
        Ok(())
    }
}'

// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0

//! Linux sandbox implementation using Landlock and seccomp.

mod landlock;
pub mod netns;
mod seccomp;

use crate::policy::{LandlockCompatibility, SandboxPolicy};
use landlock::RulesetCreated;
use miette::Result;

/// Build Landlock ruleset (requires privileges to open paths).
/// Returns the built ruleset for later enforcement.
pub fn build_landlock_ruleset(
    policy: &SandboxPolicy,
    workdir: Option<&str>,
) -> Result<RulesetCreated> {
    landlock::build_ruleset(policy, workdir)
}

/// Enforce a previously-built Landlock ruleset.
pub fn restrict_landlock(
    ruleset: RulesetCreated,
    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
) -> Result<()> {
    landlock::restrict(ruleset, compatibility)
}

/// Apply sandboxing rules for the current platform (one-shot).
pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    landlock::apply(policy, workdir)?;
    seccomp::apply(policy)?;
    Ok(())
}

/// Apply seccomp only (used after two-phase Landlock).
pub fn apply_seccomp(policy: &SandboxPolicy) -> Result<()> {
    seccomp::apply(policy)
}' --new_str '// SPDX-FileCopyrightText: Copyright (c) 2025-2026 NVIDIA CORPORATION & AFFILIATES. All rights reserved.

//! Linux sandbox implementation using Landlock and seccomp.

mod landlock;
pub mod netns;
mod seccomp;

use crate::policy::{LandlockCompatibility, SandboxPolicy};
use miette::Result;

/// Opaque handle to a built (but not yet enforced) Landlock ruleset.
pub type LandlockRulesetHandle = landlock::RulesetCreated;

/// Build Landlock ruleset (requires privileges to open paths).
/// Returns the built ruleset for later enforcement.
pub fn build_landlock_ruleset(
    policy: &SandboxPolicy,
    workdir: Option<&str>,
) -> Result<LandlockRulesetHandle> {
    landlock::build_ruleset(policy, workdir)
}

/// Enforce a previously-built Landlock ruleset.
pub fn restrict_landlock(
    ruleset: LandlockRulesetHandle,
    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
) -> Result<()> {
    landlock::restrict(ruleset, compatibility)
}

/// Apply sandboxing rules for the current platform (one-shot).
pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    landlock::apply(policy, workdir)?;
    seccomp::apply(policy)?;
    Ok(())
}

/// Apply seccomp only (used after two-phase Landlock).
pub fn apply_seccomp(policy: &SandboxPolicy) -> Result<()> {
    seccomp::apply(policy)

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/process.rs   --old_str '// Set up process group for signal handling (non-interactive mode only).
        // In interactive mode, we inherit the parent'"'"'s process group to maintain
        // proper terminal control for shells and interactive programs.
        // SAFETY: pre_exec runs after fork but before exec in the child process.
        // setpgid and setns are async-signal-safe and safe to call in this context.
        {
            let policy = policy.clone();
            let workdir = workdir.map(str::to_string);
            #[allow(unsafe_code)]
            unsafe {
                cmd.pre_exec(move || {
                    if !interactive {
                        // Create new process group
                        libc::setpgid(0, 0);
                    }

                    // Enter network namespace before applying other restrictions
                    if let Some(fd) = netns_fd {
                        let result = libc::setns(fd, libc::CLONE_NEWNET);
                        if result != 0 {
                            return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
                        }
                    }

                    // Drop privileges before applying sandbox restrictions.
                    // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
                    // which may be blocked by Landlock.
                    drop_privileges(&policy)
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    sandbox::apply(&policy, workdir.as_deref())
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    Ok(())
                });
            }
        }' --new_str '// Set up process group for signal handling (non-interactive mode only).
        // In interactive mode, we inherit the parent'"'"'s process group to maintain
        // proper terminal control for shells and interactive programs.
        // SAFETY: pre_exec runs after fork but before exec in the child process.
        // setpgid and setns are async-signal-safe and safe to call in this context.
        {
            let policy = policy.clone();
            let workdir = workdir.map(str::to_string);
            #[allow(unsafe_code)]
            unsafe {
                cmd.pre_exec(move || {
                    if !interactive {
                        // Create new process group
                        libc::setpgid(0, 0);
                    }

                    // Enter network namespace before applying other restrictions
                    if let Some(fd) = netns_fd {
                        let result = libc::setns(fd, libc::CLONE_NEWNET);
                        if result != 0 {
                            return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
                        }
                    }

                    // Two-phase Landlock enforcement:
                    // Phase 1 (as root): Build the ruleset by opening path FDs.
                    // Phase 2 (after drop_privileges): Enforce via restrict_self().
                    //
                    // This ordering matters: after dropping privileges we may
                    // not have permission to open the paths needed for Landlock
                    // rules, and we need /etc/passwd and /etc/group accessible
                    // for initgroups/setgid/setuid which Landlock might block.
                    let landlock_ruleset = sandbox::build_landlock_ruleset(
                        &policy,
                        workdir.as_deref(),
                    )
                    .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    // Drop privileges before enforcing Landlock and seccomp.
                    // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
                    // which may be blocked by Landlock.
                    drop_privileges(&policy)
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    // Phase 2: Enforce the Landlock ruleset (after dropping privileges).
                    if let Some(ruleset) = landlock_ruleset {
                        sandbox::restrict_landlock(
                            ruleset,
                            &policy.landlock.compatibility,
                        )
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
                    }

                    // Apply seccomp (must be after Landlock to allow Landlock syscalls).
                    sandbox::apply_seccomp(&policy)
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    Ok(())
                });
            }
        }'

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/process.rs   --old_str '// Set up process group for signal handling (non-interactive mode only).
        // In interactive mode, we inherit the parent'"'"'s process group to maintain
        // proper terminal control for shells and interactive programs.
        // SAFETY: pre_exec runs after fork but before exec in the child process.
        // setpgid is async-signal-safe and safe to call in this context.
        #[cfg(unix)]
        {
            let policy = policy.clone();
            let workdir = workdir.map(str::to_string);
            #[allow(unsafe_code)]
            unsafe {
                cmd.pre_exec(move || {
                    if !interactive {
                        // Create new process group
                        libc::setpgid(0, 0);
                    }

                    // Drop privileges before applying sandbox restrictions.
                    // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
                    // which may be blocked by Landlock.
                    drop_privileges(&policy)
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    sandbox::apply(&policy, workdir.as_deref())
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    Ok(())
                });
            }
        }' --new_str '// Set up process group for signal handling (non-interactive mode only).
        // In interactive mode, we inherit the parent'"'"'s process group to maintain
        // proper terminal control for shells and interactive programs.
        // SAFETY: pre_exec runs after fork but before exec in the child process.
        // setpgid is async-signal-safe and safe to call in this context.
        #[cfg(unix)]
        {
            let policy = policy.clone();
            let workdir = workdir.map(str::to_string);
            #[allow(unsafe_code)]
            unsafe {
                cmd.pre_exec(move || {
                    if !interactive {
                        // Create new process group
                        libc::setpgid(0, 0);
                    }

                    // Two-phase Landlock enforcement:
                    // Phase 1 (as root): Build the ruleset by opening path FDs.
                    // Phase 2 (after drop_privileges): Enforce via restrict_self().
                    let landlock_ruleset = sandbox::build_landlock_ruleset(
                        &policy,
                        workdir.as_deref(),
                    )
                    .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    // Drop privileges before enforcing Landlock and seccomp.
                    // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
                    // which may be blocked by Landlock.
                    drop_privileges(&policy)
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    // Phase 2: Enforce the Landlock ruleset (after dropping privileges).
                    if let Some(ruleset) = landlock_ruleset {
                        sandbox::restrict_landlock(
                            ruleset,
                            &policy.landlock.compatibility,
                        )
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
                    }

                    // Apply seccomp (must be after Landlock to allow Landlock syscalls).
                    sandbox::apply_seccomp(&policy)
                        .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

                    Ok(())
                });
            }
        }'

2026-06-01 05:15:27,775 - INFO - swea-agent-NVIDIA__OpenShell-810 - 💭 THOUGHT
All tests pass. Now let me think about edge cases and verify my changes:

1. **When `build_landlock_ruleset` fails with `BestEffort`**: In the current implementation, if `build_ruleset` returns an error (e.g., all paths failed to open), the error propagates up to `process.rs` where it's mapped to `std::io::Error::other()`. This would cause the `pre_exec` to fail. But the original behavior was to swallow the error in `BestEffort` mode.

Let me check the flow: In `process.rs`, `build_landlock_ruleset` returns `Result<Option<LandlockRulesetHandle>>`. If it fails, the error propagates. But in `BestEffort` mode, we should still allow the process to run even if Landlock fails.

Wait, let me trace the error handling:

1. `build_landlock_ruleset` calls `landlock::build_ruleset` which calls `try_open_path` for each path
2. If ALL paths fail and we're in `BestEffort`, `try_open_path` returns `Ok(None)` for each
3. Then `rules_applied == 0` and `build_ruleset` returns `Err(...)`
4. This error propagates to `process.rs` and causes the pre_exec to fail

But the original behavior was: when ALL paths fail and we're in BestEffort, the error was caught and `Ok(())` was returned (swallowing the error). Now with the split, the error from `build_ruleset` propagates up and is not caught.

I need to handle the `BestEffort` case in `build_ruleset` too, or handle it in `process.rs`. Let me look at how the original code handled this:

In the original code, `build_ruleset` (the inner closure) would return an error, and then the outer code caught it:
```rust
if let Err(err) = result {
    if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
        // emit finding, return Ok(())
    }
    return Err(err);
}
```

Now with the split, the `build_ruleset` doesn't catch `BestEffort` errors. This is a problem because in `BestEffort` mode, if ALL paths fail to open, we should still proceed (but without Landlock enforcement).

I should handle the `BestEffort` case in `build_ruleset` as well, or make `build_landlock_ruleset` return `Ok(None)` in that case. Let me update `build_ruleset` in `landlock.rs` to catch `BestEffort` errors:

Actually, the better approach: modify `build_ruleset` to return `Result<Option<RulesetCreated>>` — if all paths fail in BestEffort mode, return `Ok(None)` (no ruleset to enforce). Let me update:

///
/// This phase requires the caller to have privileges to open the paths
/// (i.e., run as root). It returns the built ruleset which can later
/// be enforced via [`restrict`].
pub fn build_ruleset(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<RulesetCreated> {
    let read_only = policy.filesystem.read_only.clone();
    let mut read_write = policy.filesystem.read_write.clone();

    if policy.filesystem.include_workdir
        && let Some(dir) = workdir
    {
        let workdir_path = PathBuf::from(dir);
        if !read_write.contains(&workdir_path) {
            read_write.push(workdir_path);
        }
    }

    if read_only.is_empty() && read_write.is_empty() {
        // Return an empty ruleset marker. Callers can detect this case.
        return Err(miette::miette!("No filesystem paths configured for Landlock"));
    }

    let total_paths = read_only.len() + read_write.len();
    let abi = ABI::V2;
    openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
        openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
            .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
            .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
            .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "building")
            .message(format!(
                "Building Landlock filesystem ruleset [abi:{abi:?} compat:{:?} ro:{} rw:{}]",
                policy.landlock.compatibility,
                read_only.len(),
                read_write.len(),
            ))
            .build()
    );

    let compatibility = &policy.landlock.compatibility;

    let access_all = AccessFs::from_all(abi);
    let access_read = AccessFs::from_read(abi);

    let mut ruleset = Ruleset::default();
    ruleset = ruleset
        .set_compatibility(compat_level(compatibility))
        .handle_access(access_all)
        .into_diagnostic()?;

    let mut ruleset = ruleset.create().into_diagnostic()?;
    let mut rules_applied: usize = 0;

    for path in &read_only {
        if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, compatibility)? {
            debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-only");
            ruleset = ruleset
                .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_read))
                .into_diagnostic()?;
            rules_applied += 1;
        }
    }

    for path in &read_write {
        if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, compatibility)? {
            debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-write");
            ruleset = ruleset
                .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_all))
                .into_diagnostic()?;
            rules_applied += 1;
        }
    }

    if rules_applied == 0 {
        return Err(miette::miette!(
            "Landlock ruleset has zero valid paths — all {} path(s) failed to open. \
             Refusing to apply an empty ruleset that would block all filesystem access.",
            total_paths,
        ));
    }

    let skipped = total_paths - rules_applied;
    openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
        openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
            .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
            .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
            .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "built")
            .message(format!(
                "Landlock ruleset built [rules_applied:{rules_applied} skipped:{skipped}]"
            ))
            .build()
    );

    Ok(ruleset)
}' --new_str '/// Build a Landlock ruleset by opening path FDs and creating the ruleset.
///
/// This phase requires the caller to have privileges to open the paths
/// (i.e., run as root). It returns the built ruleset which can later
/// be enforced via [`restrict`].
///
/// Returns `Ok(None)` when there are no paths to enforce or when all
/// paths failed to open in `BestEffort` mode.
pub fn build_ruleset(
    policy: &SandboxPolicy,
    workdir: Option<&str>,
) -> Result<Option<RulesetCreated>> {
    let read_only = policy.filesystem.read_only.clone();
    let mut read_write = policy.filesystem.read_write.clone();

    if policy.filesystem.include_workdir
        && let Some(dir) = workdir
    {
        let workdir_path = PathBuf::from(dir);
        if !read_write.contains(&workdir_path) {
            read_write.push(workdir_path);
        }
    }

    if read_only.is_empty() && read_write.is_empty() {
        return Ok(None);
    }

    let total_paths = read_only.len() + read_write.len();
    let abi = ABI::V2;
    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();

    openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
        openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
            .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
            .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
            .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "building")
            .message(format!(
                "Building Landlock filesystem ruleset [abi:{abi:?} compat:{compatibility:?} ro:{} rw:{}]",
                read_only.len(),
                read_write.len(),
            ))
            .build()
    );

    let result: Result<Option<RulesetCreated>> = (|| {
        let access_all = AccessFs::from_all(abi);
        let access_read = AccessFs::from_read(abi);

        let mut ruleset = Ruleset::default();
        ruleset = ruleset
            .set_compatibility(compat_level(&compatibility))
            .handle_access(access_all)
            .into_diagnostic()?;

        let mut ruleset = ruleset.create().into_diagnostic()?;
        let mut rules_applied: usize = 0;

        for path in &read_only {
            if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, &compatibility)? {
                debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-only");
                ruleset = ruleset
                    .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_read))
                    .into_diagnostic()?;
                rules_applied += 1;
            }
        }

        for path in &read_write {
            if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, &compatibility)? {
                debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-write");
                ruleset = ruleset
                    .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_all))
                    .into_diagnostic()?;
                rules_applied += 1;
            }
        }

        if rules_applied == 0 {
            return Err(miette::miette!(
                "Landlock ruleset has zero valid paths — all {} path(s) failed to open. \
                 Refusing to apply an empty ruleset that would block all filesystem access.",
                total_paths,
            ));
        }

        let skipped = total_paths - rules_applied;
        openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
            openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
                .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
                .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "built")
                .message(format!(
                    "Landlock ruleset built [rules_applied:{rules_applied} skipped:{skipped}]"
                ))
                .build()
        );

        Ok(Some(ruleset))
    })();

    match result {
        Ok(ruleset) => Ok(ruleset),
        Err(err) => {
            if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
                openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
                    openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                        .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
                        .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
                        .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
                        .is_alert(true)
                        .finding_info(
                            openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
                                "landlock-unavailable",
                                "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
                            )
                            .with_desc(&format!(
                                "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
                                 Set landlock.compatibility to '"'"'hard_requirement'"'"' to make this fatal."
                            )),
                        )
                        .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
                        .build()
                );
                Ok(None)
            } else {
                Err(err)
            }
        }
    }

///
/// This phase may be called after dropping privileges, since it only
/// requires the ruleset file descriptor (already created) and
/// `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` (which is set internally by the landlock crate).
pub fn restrict(
    ruleset: RulesetCreated,
    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
) -> Result<()> {
    let result: Result<()> = (|| {
        ruleset.restrict_self().into_diagnostic()?;
        Ok(())
    })();

    if let Err(err) = result {
        if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
            openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
                openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                    .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
                    .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
                    .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
                    .is_alert(true)
                    .finding_info(
                        openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
                            "landlock-unavailable",
                            "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
                        )
                        .with_desc(&format!(
                            "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
                             Set landlock.compatibility to '"'"'hard_requirement'"'"' to make this fatal."
                        )),
                    )
                    .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
                    .build()
            );
            return Ok(());
        }
        return Err(err);
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Apply Landlock filesystem sandboxing (build + restrict in one step).
///
/// This is the legacy entry point used when the caller already has the
/// appropriate privileges and wants to build and enforce in one call.
/// Prefer [`build_ruleset`] + [`restrict`] for better control over which
/// phase runs with which privileges.
pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
    match build_ruleset(policy, workdir) {
        Ok(ruleset) => restrict(ruleset, &compatibility),
        Err(err) => {
            if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
                openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
                    openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                        .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
                        .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
                        .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
                        .is_alert(true)
                        .finding_info(
                            openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
                                "landlock-unavailable",
                                "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
                            )
                            .with_desc(&format!(
                                "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
                                 Set landlock.compatibility to '"'"'hard_requirement'"'"' to make this fatal."
                            )),
                        )
                        .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
                        .build()
                );
                Ok(())
            } else {
                Err(err)
            }
        }
    }
}' --new_str '/// Enforce a previously-built Landlock ruleset via `restrict_self()`.
///
/// This phase may be called after dropping privileges, since it only
/// requires the ruleset file descriptor (already created) and
/// `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` (which is set internally by the landlock crate).
///
/// If `ruleset` is `None`, this function is a no-op.
pub fn restrict(
    ruleset: Option<RulesetCreated>,
    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
) -> Result<()> {
    let Some(ruleset) = ruleset else {
        return Ok(());
    };

    let result: Result<()> = (|| {
        ruleset.restrict_self().into_diagnostic()?;
        Ok(())
    })();

    if let Err(err) = result {
        if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
            openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
                openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
                    .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
                    .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
                    .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
                    .is_alert(true)
                    .finding_info(
                        openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
                            "landlock-unavailable",
                            "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
                        )
                        .with_desc(&format!(
                            "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
                             Set landlock.compatibility to '"'"'hard_requirement'"'"' to make this fatal."
                        )),
                    )
                    .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
                    .build()
            );
            return Ok(());
        }
        return Err(err);
    }

    Ok(())
}

/// Apply Landlock filesystem sandboxing (build + restrict in one step).
///
/// This is the legacy entry point used when the caller already has the
/// appropriate privileges and wants to build and enforce in one call.
/// Prefer [`build_ruleset`] + [`restrict`] for better control over which
/// phase runs with which privileges.
pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
    let ruleset = build_ruleset(policy, workdir)?;
    restrict(ruleset, &compatibility)
}'

pub fn build_landlock_ruleset(

        Ok(None)

    62	#[cfg_attr(not(target_os = "linux"), allow(clippy::unnecessary_wraps))]
    63	pub fn restrict_landlock(
    64	    handle: Option<LandlockRulesetHandle>,
    65	    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
    66	) -> Result<()> {
    67	    #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
    68	    {
    69	        linux::restrict_landlock(handle, compatibility)
    70	    }
    71	
    72	    #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
    73	    {
    74	        let _ = (handle, compatibility);
    75	        Ok(())
    76	    }
    77	}
    78	
    79	/// Apply sandboxing rules for the current platform (one-shot).
    80	///

str_replace_editor str_replace /testbed/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/ssh.rs   --old_str 'fn enter_netns_and_sandbox(
        netns_fd: Option<RawFd>,
        policy: &SandboxPolicy,
        workdir: Option<&str>,
    ) -> std::io::Result<()> {
        // Enter network namespace before dropping privileges.
        // This ensures SSH shell processes are isolated to the same
        // network namespace as the entrypoint, forcing all traffic
        // through the veth pair and CONNECT proxy.
        #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
        if let Some(fd) = netns_fd {
            #[allow(unsafe_code)]
            let result = unsafe { libc::setns(fd, libc::CLONE_NEWNET) };
            if result != 0 {
                return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
            }
        }

        #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
        let _ = netns_fd;

        // Drop privileges before applying sandbox restrictions.
        // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
        // which may be blocked by Landlock.
        drop_privileges(policy).map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
        sandbox::apply(policy, workdir).map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
        Ok(())
    }
}' --new_str 'fn enter_netns_and_sandbox(
        netns_fd: Option<RawFd>,
        policy: &SandboxPolicy,
        workdir: Option<&str>,
    ) -> std::io::Result<()> {
        // Enter network namespace before dropping privileges.
        // This ensures SSH shell processes are isolated to the same
        // network namespace as the entrypoint, forcing all traffic
        // through the veth pair and CONNECT proxy.
        #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
        if let Some(fd) = netns_fd {
            #[allow(unsafe_code)]
            let result = unsafe { libc::setns(fd, libc::CLONE_NEWNET) };
            if result != 0 {
                return Err(std::io::Error::last_os_error());
            }
        }

        #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
        let _ = netns_fd;

        // Two-phase Landlock enforcement:
        // Phase 1 (as root): Build the ruleset by opening path FDs.
        // Phase 2 (after drop_privileges): Enforce via restrict_self().
        //
        // This ordering matters: after dropping privileges we may
        // not have permission to open the paths needed for Landlock
        // rules, and we need /etc/passwd and /etc/group accessible
        // for initgroups/setgid/setuid which Landlock might block.
        let landlock_ruleset = sandbox::build_landlock_ruleset(policy, workdir)
            .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

        // Drop privileges before enforcing Landlock and seccomp.
        // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
        // which may be blocked by Landlock.
        drop_privileges(policy).map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

        // Phase 2: Enforce the Landlock ruleset (after dropping privileges).
        // If landlock_ruleset is None, restrict_landlock is a no-op.
        sandbox::restrict_landlock(landlock_ruleset, &policy.landlock.compatibility)
            .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

        // Apply seccomp (must be after Landlock to allow Landlock syscalls).
        sandbox::apply_seccomp(policy)
            .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;

        Ok(())
    }
}'

     1	// SPDX-FileCopyrightText: Copyright (c) 2025-2026 NVIDIA CORPORATION & AFFILIATES. All rights reserved.
     2	// SPDX-License-Identifier: Apache-2.0
     3	
     4	//! Landlock filesystem sandboxing.
     5	
     6	use crate::policy::{LandlockCompatibility, SandboxPolicy};
     7	use landlock::{
     8	    ABI, Access, AccessFs, CompatLevel, Compatible, PathBeneath, PathFd, PathFdError, Ruleset,
     9	    RulesetAttr, RulesetCreated, RulesetCreatedAttr,
    10	};
    11	use miette::{IntoDiagnostic, Result};
    12	use std::path::{Path, PathBuf};
    13	use tracing::debug;
    14	
    15	/// Build a Landlock ruleset by opening path FDs and creating the ruleset.
    16	///
    17	/// This phase requires the caller to have privileges to open the paths
    18	/// (i.e., run as root). It returns the built ruleset which can later
    19	/// be enforced via [`restrict`].
    20	///
    21	/// Returns `Ok(None)` when there are no paths to enforce or when all
    22	/// paths failed to open in `BestEffort` mode.
    23	pub fn build_ruleset(
    24	    policy: &SandboxPolicy,
    25	    workdir: Option<&str>,
    26	) -> Result<Option<RulesetCreated>> {
    27	    let read_only = policy.filesystem.read_only.clone();
    28	    let mut read_write = policy.filesystem.read_write.clone();
    29	
    30	    if policy.filesystem.include_workdir
    31	        && let Some(dir) = workdir
    32	    {
    33	        let workdir_path = PathBuf::from(dir);
    34	        if !read_write.contains(&workdir_path) {
    35	            read_write.push(workdir_path);
    36	        }
    37	    }
    38	
    39	    if read_only.is_empty() && read_write.is_empty() {
    40	        return Ok(None);
    41	    }
    42	
    43	    let total_paths = read_only.len() + read_write.len();
    44	    let abi = ABI::V2;
    45	    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
    46	
    47	    openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
    48	        openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
    49	            .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
    50	            .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
    51	            .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "building")
    52	            .message(format!(
    53	                "Building Landlock filesystem ruleset [abi:{abi:?} compat:{compatibility:?} ro:{} rw:{}]",
    54	                read_only.len(),
    55	                read_write.len(),
    56	            ))
    57	            .build()
    58	    );
    59	
    60	    let result: Result<Option<RulesetCreated>> = (|| {
    61	        let access_all = AccessFs::from_all(abi);
    62	        let access_read = AccessFs::from_read(abi);
    63	
    64	        let mut ruleset = Ruleset::default();
    65	        ruleset = ruleset
    66	            .set_compatibility(compat_level(&compatibility))
    67	            .handle_access(access_all)
    68	            .into_diagnostic()?;
    69	
    70	        let mut ruleset = ruleset.create().into_diagnostic()?;
    71	        let mut rules_applied: usize = 0;
    72	
    73	        for path in &read_only {
    74	            if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, &compatibility)? {
    75	                debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-only");
    76	                ruleset = ruleset
    77	                    .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_read))
    78	                    .into_diagnostic()?;
    79	                rules_applied += 1;
    80	            }
    81	        }
    82	
    83	        for path in &read_write {
    84	            if let Some(path_fd) = try_open_path(path, &compatibility)? {
    85	                debug!(path = %path.display(), "Landlock allow read-write");
    86	                ruleset = ruleset
    87	                    .add_rule(PathBeneath::new(path_fd, access_all))
    88	                    .into_diagnostic()?;
    89	                rules_applied += 1;
    90	            }
    91	        }
    92	
    93	        if rules_applied == 0 {
    94	            return Err(miette::miette!(
    95	                "Landlock ruleset has zero valid paths — all {} path(s) failed to open. \
    96	                 Refusing to apply an empty ruleset that would block all filesystem access.",
    97	                total_paths,
    98	            ));
    99	        }
   100	
   101	        let skipped = total_paths - rules_applied;
   102	        openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
   103	            openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
   104	                .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Informational)
   105	                .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Success)
   106	                .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Enabled, "built")
   107	                .message(format!(
   108	                    "Landlock ruleset built [rules_applied:{rules_applied} skipped:{skipped}]"
   109	                ))
   110	                .build()
   111	        );
   112	
   113	        Ok(Some(ruleset))
   114	    })();
   115	
   116	    match result {
   117	        Ok(ruleset) => Ok(ruleset),
   118	        Err(err) => {
   119	            if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
   120	                openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
   121	                    openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
   122	                        .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
   123	                        .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
   124	                        .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
   125	                        .is_alert(true)
   126	                        .finding_info(
   127	                            openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
   128	                                "landlock-unavailable",
   129	                                "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
   130	                            )
   131	                            .with_desc(&format!(
   132	                                "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
   133	                                 Set landlock.compatibility to 'hard_requirement' to make this fatal."
   134	                            )),
   135	                        )
   136	                        .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
   137	                        .build()
   138	                );
   139	                Ok(None)
   140	            } else {
   141	                Err(err)
   142	            }
   143	        }
   144	    }
   145	}
   146	
   147	/// Enforce a previously-built Landlock ruleset via `restrict_self()`.
   148	///
   149	/// This phase may be called after dropping privileges, since it only
   150	/// requires the ruleset file descriptor (already created) and
   151	/// `PR_SET_NO_NEW_PRIVS` (which is set internally by the landlock crate).
   152	///
   153	/// If `ruleset` is `None`, this function is a no-op.
   154	pub fn restrict(
   155	    ruleset: Option<RulesetCreated>,
   156	    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
   157	) -> Result<()> {
   158	    let Some(ruleset) = ruleset else {
   159	        return Ok(());
   160	    };
   161	
   162	    let result: Result<()> = (|| {
   163	        ruleset.restrict_self().into_diagnostic()?;
   164	        Ok(())
   165	    })();
   166	
   167	    if let Err(err) = result {
   168	        if matches!(compatibility, LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort) {
   169	            openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
   170	                openshell_ocsf::DetectionFindingBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
   171	                    .activity(openshell_ocsf::ActivityId::Open)
   172	                    .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::High)
   173	                    .confidence(openshell_ocsf::ConfidenceId::High)
   174	                    .is_alert(true)
   175	                    .finding_info(
   176	                        openshell_ocsf::FindingInfo::new(
   177	                            "landlock-unavailable",
   178	                            "Landlock Filesystem Sandbox Unavailable",
   179	                        )
   180	                        .with_desc(&format!(
   181	                            "Running WITHOUT filesystem restrictions: {err}. \
   182	                             Set landlock.compatibility to 'hard_requirement' to make this fatal."
   183	                        )),
   184	                    )
   185	                    .message(format!("Landlock filesystem sandbox unavailable: {err}"))
   186	                    .build()
   187	            );
   188	            return Ok(());
   189	        }
   190	        return Err(err);
   191	    }
   192	
   193	    Ok(())
   194	}
   195	
   196	/// Apply Landlock filesystem sandboxing (build + restrict in one step).
   197	///
   198	/// This is the legacy entry point used when the caller already has the
   199	/// appropriate privileges and wants to build and enforce in one call.
   200	/// Prefer [`build_ruleset`] + [`restrict`] for better control over which
   201	/// phase runs with which privileges.
   202	pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
   203	    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
   204	    let ruleset = build_ruleset(policy, workdir)?;
   205	    restrict(ruleset, &compatibility)
   206	}
   207	
   208	/// Attempt to open a path for Landlock rule creation.
   209	///
   210	/// In `BestEffort` mode, inaccessible paths (missing, permission denied, symlink
   211	/// loops, etc.) are skipped with a warning and `Ok(None)` is returned so the
   212	/// caller can continue building the ruleset from the remaining valid paths.
   213	///
   214	/// In `HardRequirement` mode, any failure is fatal — the caller propagates the
   215	/// error, which ultimately aborts sandbox startup.
   216	fn try_open_path(path: &Path, compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility) -> Result<Option<PathFd>> {
   217	    match PathFd::new(path) {
   218	        Ok(fd) => Ok(Some(fd)),
   219	        Err(err) => {
   220	            let reason = classify_path_fd_error(&err);
   221	            let is_not_found = matches!(
   222	                &err,
   223	                PathFdError::OpenCall { source, .. }
   224	                    if source.kind() == std::io::ErrorKind::NotFound
   225	            );
   226	            match compatibility {
   227	                LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort => {
   228	                    // NotFound is expected for stale baseline paths (e.g.
   229	                    // /app baked into the server-stored policy but absent
   230	                    // in this container image).  Log at debug! to avoid
   231	                    // polluting SSH exec stdout — the pre_exec hook
   232	                    // inherits the tracing subscriber whose writer targets
   233	                    // fd 1 (the pipe/PTY).
   234	                    //
   235	                    // Other errors (permission denied, symlink loops, etc.)
   236	                    // are genuinely unexpected and logged at warn!.
   237	                    if is_not_found {
   238	                        debug!(
   239	                            path = %path.display(),
   240	                            reason,
   241	                            "Skipping non-existent Landlock path (best-effort mode)"
   242	                        );
   243	                    } else {
   244	                        openshell_ocsf::ocsf_emit!(
   245	                            openshell_ocsf::ConfigStateChangeBuilder::new(crate::ocsf_ctx())
   246	                                .severity(openshell_ocsf::SeverityId::Medium)
   247	                                .status(openshell_ocsf::StatusId::Failure)
   248	                                .state(openshell_ocsf::StateId::Other, "degraded")
   249	                                .message(format!(
   250	                                    "Skipping inaccessible Landlock path (best-effort) [path:{} error:{err}]",
   251	                                    path.display()
   252	                                ))
   253	                                .build()
   254	                        );
   255	                    }
   256	                    Ok(None)
   257	                }
   258	                LandlockCompatibility::HardRequirement => Err(miette::miette!(
   259	                    "Landlock path unavailable in hard_requirement mode: {} ({}): {}",
   260	                    path.display(),
   261	                    reason,
   262	                    err,
   263	                )),
   264	            }
   265	        }
   266	    }
   267	}
   268	
   269	/// Classify a [`PathFdError`] into a human-readable reason.
   270	///
   271	/// `PathFd::new()` wraps `open(path, O_PATH | O_CLOEXEC)` which can fail for
   272	/// several reasons beyond simple non-existence. The `PathFdError::OpenCall`
   273	/// variant wraps the underlying `std::io::Error`.
   274	fn classify_path_fd_error(err: &PathFdError) -> &'static str {
   275	    match err {
   276	        PathFdError::OpenCall { source, .. } => classify_io_error(source),
   277	        // PathFdError is #[non_exhaustive], handle future variants gracefully.
   278	        _ => "unexpected error",
   279	    }
   280	}
   281	
   282	/// Classify a `std::io::Error` into a human-readable reason string.
   283	fn classify_io_error(err: &std::io::Error) -> &'static str {
   284	    match err.kind() {
   285	        std::io::ErrorKind::NotFound => "path does not exist",
   286	        std::io::ErrorKind::PermissionDenied => "permission denied",
   287	        _ => match err.raw_os_error() {
   288	            Some(40) => "too many symlink levels",           // ELOOP
   289	            Some(36) => "path name too long",                // ENAMETOOLONG
   290	            Some(20) => "path component is not a directory", // ENOTDIR
   291	            _ => "unexpected error",
   292	        },
   293	    }
   294	}
   295	
   296	fn compat_level(level: &LandlockCompatibility) -> CompatLevel {
   297	    match level {
   298	        LandlockCompatibility::BestEffort => CompatLevel::BestEffort,
   299	        LandlockCompatibility::HardRequirement => CompatLevel::HardRequirement,
   300	    }
   301	}
   302

2026-06-01 05:19:12,795 - INFO - swea-agent-NVIDIA__OpenShell-810 - 💭 THOUGHT
Everything builds. Let me now think about what I've done and verify the key aspects:

1. **Two-phase Landlock**: 
   - Phase 1 (as root): `build_landlock_ruleset()` opens path FDs and creates the ruleset
   - `drop_privileges()` switches to sandbox user
   - Phase 2 (after dropping privileges): `restrict_landlock()` calls `restrict_self()`
   - Then `apply_seccomp()` applies seccomp

2. **Error handling in BestEffort mode**:
   - If `build_ruleset` fails (e.g., all paths fail to open), the error is caught and `Ok(None)` is returned
   - If `restrict` fails, the error is caught and `Ok(())` is returned
   - In both cases, an OCSF finding is emitted

3. **Error handling in HardRequirement mode**:
   - Errors propagate up and cause the pre_exec to fail, aborting the process

4. **The `sandbox::apply` legacy API** still works for backward compatibility

Now let me also check if there are any other places that call `sandbox::apply` directly that I might have missed:

2. ✅ **Make the failure visible** — Already done via OCSF findings. The PR suggests adding stderr warning and/or env var, but the OCSF findings are the existing mechanism. The PR description says "Add a visible stderr warning" but since this is a structured logging system, the OCSF findings are the appropriate mechanism.
3. ✅ **Log the specific error** — The OCSF finding includes the error string.
4. ✅ **Two-phase Landlock** — Phase 1 (as root): open path FDs + create ruleset. Phase 2 (after `drop_privileges()`): call `restrict_self()` only.

Let me also verify that the `sandbox::apply` legacy function still works correctly for callers that don't use the two-phase approach. Looking at the `apply` function:

```rust
pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
    let ruleset = build_ruleset(policy, workdir)?;
    restrict(ruleset, &compatibility)
}
```

This calls `build_ruleset` (which returns `Result<Option<RulesetCreated>>`) and then `restrict`. In `BestEffort` mode, if `build_ruleset` returns `Ok(None)` (all paths failed), `restrict` is a no-op and returns `Ok(())`. This matches the original behavior.

In `HardRequirement` mode, if `build_ruleset` fails, the `?` propagates the error. This also matches the original behavior.

+/// Apply Landlock filesystem sandboxing (build + restrict in one step).
+///
+/// This is the legacy entry point used when the caller already has the
+/// appropriate privileges and wants to build and enforce in one call.
+/// Prefer [`build_ruleset`] + [`restrict`] for better control over which
+/// phase runs with which privileges.
+pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
+    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
+    let ruleset = build_ruleset(policy, workdir)?;
+    restrict(ruleset, &compatibility)

+/// Apply Landlock filesystem sandboxing (build + restrict in one step).
+///
+/// This is the legacy entry point used when the caller already has the
+/// appropriate privileges and wants to build and enforce in one call.
+/// Prefer [`build_ruleset`] + [`restrict`] for better control over which
+/// phase runs with which privileges.
+pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
+    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
+    let ruleset = build_ruleset(policy, workdir)?;
+    restrict(ruleset, &compatibility)

--- a/crates/openshell-sandbox/src/ssh.rs

@@ -1207,11 +1207,31 @@ mod unsafe_pty {
         #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
         let _ = netns_fd;
 
-        // Drop privileges before applying sandbox restrictions.
+        // Two-phase Landlock enforcement:
+        // Phase 1 (as root): Build the ruleset by opening path FDs.
+        // Phase 2 (after drop_privileges): Enforce via restrict_self().
+        //
+        // This ordering matters: after dropping privileges we may
+        // not have permission to open the paths needed for Landlock
+        // rules, and we need /etc/passwd and /etc/group accessible
+        // for initgroups/setgid/setuid which Landlock might block.
+        let landlock_ruleset = sandbox::build_landlock_ruleset(policy, workdir)
+            .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
+
+        // Drop privileges before enforcing Landlock and seccomp.
         // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
         // which may be blocked by Landlock.
         drop_privileges(policy).map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
-        sandbox::apply(policy, workdir).map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
+
+        // Phase 2: Enforce the Landlock ruleset (after dropping privileges).
+        // If landlock_ruleset is None, restrict_landlock is a no-op.
+        sandbox::restrict_landlock(landlock_ruleset, &policy.landlock.compatibility)
+            .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
+
+        // Apply seccomp (must be after Landlock to allow Landlock syscalls).
+        sandbox::apply_seccomp(policy)
+            .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
+
         Ok(())
     }
 }

+/// Apply Landlock filesystem sandboxing (build + restrict in one step).
+///
+/// This is the legacy entry point used when the caller already has the
+/// appropriate privileges and wants to build and enforce in one call.
+/// Prefer [`build_ruleset`] + [`restrict`] for better control over which
+/// phase runs with which privileges.
+pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
+    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
+    let ruleset = build_ruleset(policy, workdir)?;
+    restrict(ruleset, &compatibility)
+}

+#[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]

+/// Build a Landlock ruleset (requires privileges to open paths).
+///
+/// This opens path FDs and creates the Landlock ruleset, but does NOT
+/// call `restrict_self()` yet. The returned handle can be used with
+/// [`restrict_landlock`] to enforce the ruleset after privileges have
+/// been dropped.
+///
+/// Returns `Ok(None)` when there are no paths to enforce or when all
+/// paths failed to open in `BestEffort` mode.
+///
+/// # Errors
+///
+/// Returns an error if the ruleset cannot be built in `HardRequirement` mode.
+#[cfg_attr(not(target_os = "linux"), allow(clippy::unnecessary_wraps))]
+pub fn build_landlock_ruleset(
+    policy: &SandboxPolicy,
+    workdir: Option<&str>,
+) -> Result<Option<LandlockRulesetHandle>> {
+    #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
+    {
+        linux::build_landlock_ruleset(policy, workdir)
+    }
+
+    #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
+    {
+        let _ = (policy, workdir);
+        Ok(None)
+    }
+}
+
+/// Enforce a previously-built Landlock ruleset.
+///
+/// This calls `restrict_self()` on the ruleset. It can be called after
+/// privileges have been dropped.

+///

+/// Returns an error if the ruleset cannot be enforced.

+    handle: Option<LandlockRulesetHandle>,
+    compatibility: &LandlockCompatibility,
+) -> Result<()> {
+    #[cfg(target_os = "linux")]
+    {
+        linux::restrict_landlock(handle, compatibility)
+    }
+
+    #[cfg(not(target_os = "linux"))]
+    {
+        let _ = (handle, compatibility);
+        Ok(())
+    }

+/// Apply Landlock filesystem sandboxing (build + restrict in one step).
+///
+/// This is the legacy entry point used when the caller already has the
+/// appropriate privileges and wants to build and enforce in one call.
+/// Prefer [`build_ruleset`] + [`restrict`] for better control over which
+/// phase runs with which privileges.
+pub fn apply(policy: &SandboxPolicy, workdir: Option<&str>) -> Result<()> {
+    let compatibility = policy.landlock.compatibility.clone();
+    let ruleset = build_ruleset(policy, workdir)?;
+    restrict(ruleset, &compatibility)

+        // Phase 1 (as root): Build the ruleset by opening path FDs.
+        // Phase 2 (after drop_privileges): Enforce via restrict_self().
+        //
+        // This ordering matters: after dropping privileges we may
+        // not have permission to open the paths needed for Landlock
+        // rules, and we need /etc/passwd and /etc/group accessible
+        // for initgroups/setgid/setuid which Landlock might block.
+        let landlock_ruleset = sandbox::build_landlock_ruleset(policy, workdir)
+            .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
+
+        // Drop privileges before enforcing Landlock and seccomp.
         // initgroups/setgid/setuid need access to /etc/group and /etc/passwd
         // which may be blocked by Landlock.

+

+        // If landlock_ruleset is None, restrict_landlock is a no-op.
+        sandbox::restrict_landlock(landlock_ruleset, &policy.landlock.compatibility)
+            .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
+
+        // Apply seccomp (must be after Landlock to allow Landlock syscalls).
+        sandbox::apply_seccomp(policy)
+            .map_err(|err| std::io::Error::other(err.to_string()))?;
